{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"Productivity Champ Spotlight — Identifying Your Khakis by Branden George","link":"http://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=15960","description":"<p class=\"p1\">Branden is a member of Asian Efficiency’s online productivity community, <a href=\"https://store.asianefficiency.com/dojo/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the Dojo.</a> When he’s not helping other members, he’s focused on growing his business.</p><p>After college, Branden pursued the less traditional route which brought him to where he is today. He is the co-founder of a bar consulting company. He manages sales, marketing, and data for a procurement software startup. He also manages his parents&#8217; automotive parts business and still has time to consult clients on scaling their sales and marketing efforts with automation systems.</p><p>Read on and find out how the AE community has helped Branden achieve his goals and why he is this month’s productivity champ.</p><h2>Introducing Branden George</h2><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-15373\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/Branden_George.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"603\" height=\"603\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/Branden_George.jpg 603w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/Branden_George-240x240.jpg 240w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/Branden_George-500x500.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/Branden_George-150x150.jpg 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 603px) 100vw, 603px\" /></p><p><strong><em>Tell us a little bit about who you are and what you’re up to.</em></strong></p><p>Day-to-day I manage marketing, data, and tech for a software startup. I&#8217;m also co-founder of a bar consulting and staffing company. I&#8217;m gradually taking over operations for my Dad&#8217;s auto parts business, and I do some marketing and automation consulting on the side.</p><p>In my downtime, I try to eat enough to stay alive.</p><p><strong><em>What is the backstory that ignited you to get started on becoming more productive?</em></strong></p><p>It isn&#8217;t so much a well-defined backstory as it is a tale of gradual self-awareness that, humorously, mirrors the stages of grief.</p><ol><li>Denial &#8211; I&#8217;m fine. I&#8217;ll just work late. I&#8217;ll catch up on the weekend.</li><li>Anger &#8211; Why am I so busy but nothing gets done? I&#8217;m sick of running in place!</li><li>Bargaining &#8211; I&#8217;ll sell my soul for enough magic to tackle 1/2 of my to-do list overnight.</li><li>Depression &#8211; Maybe it&#8217;s me. Maybe I just don&#8217;t have the drive or focus of my peers. I can&#8217;t change the fact that I&#8217;m ADHD.</li><li>Acceptance &#8211; Maybe, just maybe, productivity is a skill that can be learned.</li></ol><p><em><strong>What was the wall or problem that you ran into that stopped you from accomplishing what you wanted?</strong></em></p><p>I identified with my khakis.</p><p><em><strong>What was the epiphany you experienced and discovered?</strong></em></p><p>&#8220;You are not the contents of your wallet. You are not your (expletive) khakis.&#8221; Ah &#8211; one of my all-time favorite quotes. While that Fight Club line is open to interpretation, to me, the obvious conclusion is that you shouldn&#8217;t build an identity based on material possessions.</p><p>Several years ago, in a completely unrelated conversation, I asked my friend Jessica about her work as a speech therapist. I used the phrase &#8220;autistic child&#8221;. She immediately corrected me. &#8220;We say a child with autism. You don&#8217;t define someone by their condition.</p><p>&#8220;The slight change of phrasing caught me off guard. The lightbulb went off. I began to see a deeper meaning in Fight Club. We&#8217;re not the collective sum of our possessions, nor are we defined by our condition in life. I realized that I defined myself by my ADHD and my seemingly inherent disorganization.</p><p><em><strong>What was the transformation that you experienced?</strong></em></p><p>I was freed from paralysis. 2 years ago I was wallowing in self-pity, largely living off my parents&#8217; generosity. Today I&#8217;m proud of starting 2 profitable businesses, proud to be able to continue my Dad&#8217;s business, and proud to have a day job with an incredible team. The best part? I do it all from home in my PJs.</p><p><em><strong>If you have one piece of productivity advice for someone who is struggling to make progress towards their goals, what would it be?</strong></em></p><p>Wherever you&#8217;re at just remember 1) productivity is a skill that can be learned and 2) you are not your khakis. You&#8217;re not defined or limited by your challenges or situation in life. What defines you is your ability to overcome those obstacles and make your dreams a reality. It all starts with your mindset. The rest can be taught.</p><p>Thank you, Branden, for sharing!</p><p>Branden is a great example of what we refer to in our community as a “productivity champ” — someone who continuously looks for ways to become better or someone who has a <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/171-growth-mindset/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">growth mindset</a>. Other examples of people who have succeeded are <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/case-study-lisa/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Lisa</a> and <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/case-study-scott/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Scott</a> who we have written case studies about.</p><p>If you are feeling overwhelmed, exhausted, or distracted, you can overcome that and become a productivity champ too:</p><ul><li>Review our <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/tea-framework/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TEA Framework</a>, and become familiar with the <strong>3 Pillars of Productivity</strong>.</li><li>Take our super-quick <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/quiz/\" calendar to implement it.</li></ul><p>If you think we should feature you as a productivity champ, <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/contact/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">get in 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"Work From Home Challenge Day 3: Create Time And Space To Focus","link":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=16024","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16026\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/focus-page.jpg\" alt=\"Focus\" width=\"1200\" height=\"643\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/focus-page.jpg 1200w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/focus-page-500x268.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/focus-page-768x412.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/focus-page-640x343.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" /></p><p>Welcome to Day 3 of the 5-day Work From Home Challenge. If you haven’t yet, make sure you complete <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/work-from-home-day-2-daily-reset/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Day 2</a> to create the right mindset and environment for working from home.</p><p>Now that you’re set up, today’s challenge is all about making time to work on the important things you need to do. It’s not easy at the best of times, but it’s even more difficult when you’re at home!</p><h2>The Invisible Triggers</h2><p>You may not realize this, but when you go to work at an office, your day is filled with invisible triggers telling you that it is time to work.</p><p>Get in the car or on the train? Enter the building? Get in the elevator? Grab your hot beverage? Sit down at your desk and start up your computer?</p><p>All triggers that you are (or at least <em>should</em>) be switching from home mode to work mode.</p><p>Coworkers heading to the food court for lunch? Trigger for break mode.</p><p>Walking back into the building <em>after</em> lunch? Trigger to get back to work.</p><p>Time to catch your train home and coworkers packing up? Trigger to wrap it up and head home.</p><p>This can all go out the window when you work from home. You don’t have these built-in triggers and time buckets to get work done and make progress on projects and goals.</p><h2>The problem with working from home &#8211; distractions!</h2><p>Here are just a few things that are working against you when you work from home:</p><ul><li>Family members in the house with you</li><li>Laundry, dishes, and assorted housework you see when you walk through the house</li><li>People not understanding that you’re <em>working</em>, and not just on an enforced vacation</li><li>Random FaceTimes from out of town relatives stuck at home too</li><li>No coworkers around that can see your screen, so no extrinsic pressure not to slack off</li><li>All communication moved to Slack, Microsoft Teams, and Zoom. So your day becomes a never-ending barrage of coworker DMs, @mentions, and Zoom meetings</li></ul><p>If you don’t take proactive measures, your day can slip away from you. Sure, you’ve been busy, but what have you accomplished?</p><h2>Be intentional with your time</h2><p>The key is to be intentional with your time. To know what you should be working on today, and then making time to actually work on it. Then, you need to defend yourself against distractions during that time.</p><h3>Know what you should be working on</h3><p>If you’re not careful, you will end up spending your day putting out fires and dealing with whatever urgent issue has popped up this week.</p><p>Sure they’re urgent, but are they important?</p><p>What about the things that are important but aren’t screaming for your attention right now? Will you get to them “when you can?”</p><p>(Spoiler alert — that time will never come.)</p><p>If you’ve spent time reading the AE blog in the past, you’ll be familiar with this image, called <em>The Eisenhower Box</em> or <em>The Eisenhower Matrix</em>:</p> <figure><img src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/eisenhowerbox.png\" /></figure><p>When you look at your week, the key is maximizing the time spent in the top-right of the matrix. To be working on things that are important, but not hugely urgent.</p><p>When you evaluate your week and your day, you want to try to prioritize those “important but not urgent” activities and create the time to do them consistently.</p><h3>Make time to work on your important activities</h3><p>Here’s how you make sure you have time for your important activities: put them on your calendar now, or when you are planning your week and your day.</p><p>These are called <strong>focus blocks</strong>.</p><p>Not just put them on your calendar, but do what you need to do to make sure that when the time comes, you stop what you are doing and switch over to your scheduled activity.</p><p>It can be tempting to not treat these focus blocks as “real” appointments, because they are appointments with yourself. If you skip the appointment, who is going to know?</p><p>As you practice keeping these focus blocks and treating them seriously, you’ll be building the muscle and creating a habit that says: the appointments I make with myself are the most important ones of the day.</p><p>Maybe you do this with alerts all over the place. Perhaps you do it with accountability — have a friend or colleague check in with you and see if you accomplished what you said you would. Do whatever you need to do.</p><p>Here’s an example: let’s say you have a focus block scheduled this morning to write an article about working at home and focus.</p><p>And let’s say (hypothetically *cough*) that a colleague pings you and asks you to review a PDF they made.</p><p>What do you do? You want to be helpful, and clearly, people are waiting for that PDF.</p><p>If writing that article is your important task for the day, and if you have time blocked off for it, then one approach is to say:</p><p>“I’m happy to review the PDF. But I’m tied up with something right now, but I’ll be able to get to it in an hour. Will that work?”</p><p>If an hour works, great. If not, they can hopefully get someone else to do it. If there is no one else, then you can decide whether you want to stick to your focus block (the ideal situation), or if you have to review it now (not perfect, but it happens sometimes!) At least then it is an intentional choice.</p><p><em>We have more strategies for dealing with distractions when working from home coming up in a new resource we’re building. If you want to hear more about that, make sure you enter your details in the box below if you haven’t already.</em></p><h2>Exercise</h2><ul><li>Look at your calendar for the rest of the week.</li><li>Put a focus block on the calendar of at least 30 minutes as soon as you can. Tomorrow is best.</li><li>Repeat for the rest of the week.</li><li>Let us know in the comments when you’re done!</li></ul><div class=\"post-optin-wrapper\"><div class=\"inline-fields short-fields https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/success-1123017_1920-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/success-1123017_1920-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1920px) 100vw, 1920px\" /></p><p>The greatest stories of all time didn&#8217;t start and end with &#8216;and they lived happily ever after&#8217;. It&#8217;s true for us too. Our life&#8217;s story is made great by how we managed to pull ourselves up.</p><p>Talking about failures is not easy especially if it&#8217;s personal. It&#8217;s harder to talk about if you&#8217;ve not managed to rise above it. This is a topic that hits very close to home because I&#8217;ve had my share of failures to fill out an entire sheet of paper. Perhaps even more.</p><p>Whatever type of failure you go through, one thing is for certain&#8211;your initial feeling is that of helplessness and &#8220;oh sh*t&#8221; moments. There might have been times when you ended up just lying on your bed and just staring into open space and not being productive at all. I get it. I&#8217;ve been there more than once. You then experience a lul wherein you just don&#8217;t feel like doing anything. It&#8217;s normal. Give yourself that time. But do not dwell on that feeling for too long. You need to get yourself out of that rut and be better than yesterday.</p><p>Here in Asian Efficiency, we&#8217;ve helped over 13,000 people become productive but that didn&#8217;t happen overnight. It took us years to get to where we are and we&#8217;ve had our share of failures too. Over the years, we&#8217;ve learned, as a team, some strategies that you can also use to bounce back from failure. These are also strategies that we have personally used, not just in Asian Efficiency but also in our personal lives.</p><h2>What are failures?</h2><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16103 size-full\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/man-in-blue-and-brown-plaid-dress-shirt-touching-his-hair-897817.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"5760\" height=\"3840\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/man-in-blue-and-brown-plaid-dress-shirt-touching-his-hair-897817.jpg 5760w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/man-in-blue-and-brown-plaid-dress-shirt-touching-his-hair-897817-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/man-in-blue-and-brown-plaid-dress-shirt-touching-his-hair-897817-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/man-in-blue-and-brown-plaid-dress-shirt-touching-his-hair-897817-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 5760px) 100vw, 5760px\" /></p><p>You have set out to do something and you ended up not reaching it is the simplest way to describe what a failure is. My first BIG failure was setting out a goal to earn my degree in 4 years but instead, it took me 5.5 years. It might not mean a lot at first glance but it meant losing my scholarship. I was a straight-A student and was part of my university&#8217;s honor roll and in just one semester, I just decided to drop my system administration class. I don&#8217;t even remember why but I do remember the feeling of regret that followed and living through the consequences after. I was 18 and already feeling like a total failure&#8211;that nothing could top that. How wrong I was.</p><p>We all have our idea of success. We have it ingrained in our brains since we were young. It starts when our parents would tell us what they would like us to be when we grow up. Then when we&#8217;re older, our idea of success is reaching our dreams. What we lacked is the idea of failure because it&#8217;s something that we don&#8217;t want to talk about.</p><p>&#8220;Failure is not an option.&#8221; We hear this quite a lot. It might not be an option for you and me, but it doesn&#8217;t mean that it&#8217;s never going to happen. It has happened to very successful people like Steve Jobs, Mark Zuckerberg, JK Rowling, Walt Disney, and so many more. When you think about those people I have just mentioned, you don&#8217;t think about their failures because their success is so much bigger than their failures. That there is your true option&#8211;to be bigger than your failure.</p><h2>Here are 3 simple strategies on how you can bounce back from failure</h2><h3>1. Do not let your failure define who you are</h3><p>Simply put, you are not your failure. Do not dwell or beat yourself up when you fail. It happens even to the best of us. Instead of telling yourself &#8220;If only I did this&#8221;, tell yourself &#8220;Next time, here&#8217;s what I&#8217;m going to do.&#8221; The difference between the two phrases is worlds apart. One focuses on the failure while the other focuses on opportunities for growth.</p><p>When you let your failure get the best of you, this is when you feel pathetic that you are not capable of succeeding. It paralyzes you into doing nothing. So you lost a promotion to someone else. Does that mean that you shouldn&#8217;t aim for that next promotion? Of course not. It should mean that there are some things that you still need to work on or areas for improvement. You weren&#8217;t able to sign on a client? Ok. Work on the next one and see what you can improve on.</p><p>Just because you failed once doesn&#8217;t mean that you will fail the next time. Failure teaches us that there is a way for us to improve.</p><h3>2. Make changes to your environment</h3><p>When you make changes to your environment, the people you hang out with, the places you go, the music you listen to, helps rewire your brain. It can help you see things in a different light.</p><p>Take time to work outside your usual working environment. Do your thinking time in a park or work from a coffee shop or public library. Make that change.</p><p>Talk to people who might have experienced the same failure as you. Ask them how they managed to turn things around and if they are not there yet, figure it out together.</p><p>Did you go through a bad break up (or even an okay one)? Go to a new place to eat. Don&#8217;t go back to the usual places or else you&#8217;re just going to mope.</p><h3>3. Strive to be happy</h3><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16102 size-full\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/group-of-people-having-fun-together-under-the-sun-708392.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"5090\" height=\"3393\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/group-of-people-having-fun-together-under-the-sun-708392.jpg 5090w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/group-of-people-having-fun-together-under-the-sun-708392-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/group-of-people-having-fun-together-under-the-sun-708392-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/group-of-people-having-fun-together-under-the-sun-708392-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 5090px) 100vw, 5090px\" /></p><p>Happy people are productive people. This is arguably one of Thanh&#8217;s favorite phrases because it&#8217;s true. The happier you are the more productive you&#8217;ll be.</p><p>You might think that it&#8217;s impossible to be happy after failing at something. It is impossible if you manage to forget the things that make you happy.</p><p>Let&#8217;s start with this question: what makes you happy?</p><p>Whatever those are will be one of the reasons why you will bounce back from failure. More than a decade ago, my friends and I decided to build our own BPO. Unfortunately, our investors backed out during our 2nd year and we had to close it down. I was in a rut for two months. I would have to admit that I didn&#8217;t handle it well. I isolated myself from the people who mattered most. When I finally got tired feeling pathetic, I reached out to my friends. They were my happiness (still are). Finding my happiness brought me to where I am right now.</p><p>Things happen for a reason. That reason is growth. Each failure is a chance for growth. Embrace it and bounce back.</p><h2>Next steps</h2><p>Write down what makes you happy and put it somewhere that you can see every single day. Remember, when you&#8217;re happy you are productive.</p> ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 02 Jun 2020 11:00:48 +0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/success-1123017_1920.jpg","linkMd5":"24c6156d9ebee3bf6b32c415cb606670","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn38@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-12-112_65501fef9b66279e.webp","destWidth":1920,"destHeight":1280,"sourceBytes":323932,"destBytes":50636,"author":"Marmel Becerial","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/success-1123017_1920.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn38@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-12-112_65501fef9b66279e.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/man-in-blue-and-brown-plaid-dress-shirt-touching-his-hair-897817.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn92@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-51-227_c160e04b9d84e53f.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/group-of-people-having-fun-together-under-the-sun-708392.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn8@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-53-447_ade3e1a397419c86.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317508239},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"Are You Making This GTD Mistake?","link":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=16261","description":"<p><img src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/thanh-gtd.jpg\" /></p><p>I first learned about GTD back in 2008 when I picked up a paperback at the local bookstore. A few weeks earlier I got promoted at work and I was overwhelmed. Deadlines were getting missed, my workload went up and I had no way of handling this.</p><p>Then I remembered my uncle, a successful entrepreneur, telling me about GTD and how it helped him. He was someone I looked up to so I decided to get my own copy of <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/gtd-book/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Getting Things Done</a> by David Allen.</p><p>It helped me get a system place for handling my day-to-day. For the first time since my promotion, I was on top of everything and I felt like I had a new superpower.</p><p>Fast forward to today, after starting Asian Efficiency, <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/task-management/gtd-intro/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">I&#8217;ve learned a lot about the GTD methodology</a>. I was a purist for a few years until I developed my own productivity system that we now teach to our clients. Through Asian Efficiency, we&#8217;ve helped thousands of people be more successful with the Getting Things Done methodology.</p><p>After helping so many clients we&#8217;ve noticed that there&#8217;s one common mistake that we see most new GTD users make. Are you making this mistake?</p><h3>#1 Mistake New GTD Users Make</h3><p>Many years ago, I met this smart and beautiful woman in Las Vegas. We were both single and flirting with each other. She asked me what I did for a living and I said that I was blogging about productivity.</p><p>&#8220;You must be a GTD user too,&#8221; she said.</p><p>&#8220;Yes, I am. I doubt you are.&#8221;</p><p>Playfully she replied, &#8220;Excuse me? Are you doubting me that I don&#8217;t know what GTD is?&#8221;</p><p>&#8220;Yes I do. What&#8217;s the most important step in Getting Things Done?&#8221;</p><p>Only someone who is a GTD practitioner and follows the methodology on a regular basis would be able to answer this question. A few seconds later, she said:</p><p>&#8220;It&#8217;s the review step. Without it, the whole system falls apart.&#8221;</p><p>(That&#8217;s when I fell in love with this woman. We ended up dating for a few years.)</p><p>She&#8217;s right. The review step, which sometimes is referred to as the Reflect step, is the most important step of the whole GTD framework. Without it, you cannot be on top of everything that&#8217;s going on. Especially if you&#8217;re in a situation where you have many things going on at work, hundreds of emails to deal with, and many meetings to attend.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/task-management/quick-capture-primer/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">It&#8217;s easy for pieces of information, tasks, and reminders to get scattered all over the place</a>. Organizing that is important (which is why it&#8217;s one of the steps in GTD) but reviewing everything is crucial to get yourself focused on the right things coming ahead of you.</p><p><img src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/06/David-Allen-and-Thanh-Pham-480x640.jpg\" /></p><p>The biggest mistake I see that new Getting Things Done users make is that they are not consistently doing their reviews. Out of the five steps in the GTD methodology, this is the most neglected step. Without the review step, you might end up focusing your time and energy on the wrong thing. That&#8217;s not productive, is it?</p><p>So why do people struggle with this step so much? Based on my experience, there are a couple of reasons why:</p><ul><li>It can be very tedious the first few times you do it</li><li>It can take a long time to do (an hour or two)</li><li>You have to make it a habit <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/149-gtd-setup/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">which is already hard to do on top of everything else you have to learn</a></li></ul><p>The tricky thing with the review step, which the book recommends you do weekly, is that when you skip it you don&#8217;t immediately see the negative effects of it. The flip side is also true when you do review your projects and lists you feel temporarily that you have a grasp of what&#8217;s coming up. However, that feeling might only last a few minutes and then it&#8217;s gone. So you might not make it habitual because you don&#8217;t see the big benefit of it.</p><p>When you skip it a few times and don&#8217;t experience any repercussions, it&#8217;s easy to keep on skipping it and not realize you&#8217;re slowly getting to a place of overwhelm. It&#8217;s a slow process that will creep up on you.</p><p>Once you hit the tipping point that&#8217;s when you feel overwhelmed, deadlines are getting missed, and you start to procrastinate more often. You hit the point of wanting to do &#8220;<a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/116-getting-things-done-mistakes/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">GTD all over again</a>&#8221; because your projects, lists, and inbox are cluttered and all over the place.</p><p>That could have all been prevented when you did your review regularly. You have to think of it as cleaning your home on a regular basis. If you don&#8217;t do it you can still be a clean freak but eventually, it&#8217;ll get messy.</p><p>Imagine that you want to have people come over for dinner. What do you do? You probably start cleaning first, putting stuff away, organizing your home, and making sure everything is in the right place before you start cooking and setting the dinner table.</p><p>Imagine for a moment that you already had a clean house. Everything was dusted, there are no clothes on the floor and the dishes were clean. Wouldn&#8217;t it be easier, stress-free, and more fun to start preparing for dinner and having friends come over?</p><p>That&#8217;s possible for your life too when you regularly review everything. You don&#8217;t have to do all the cleaning, moving, and organizing before you do think about how to have a fun dinner party. It&#8217;s already nice and tidy! All you have to focus on is to &#8220;do the work&#8221; and you make it easy for your future-self to get started. No more procrastination, feeling overwhelmed or feeling behind.</p><p>Now you&#8217;re on top of everything and you can focus on what matters in front of you.</p><h3>How Often Should You Review?</h3><p><img src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/gtd-640x511.png\" /></p><p>To continue the house cleaning analogy, some people are messier than others. Personally, I&#8217;m a very messy person which is why I have a housekeeper coming by every week. Without her help, my place would look like a refugee camp where my parents were in the 80s.</p><p>(Fun fact: I was born in a refugee camp in the Philippines after my parents escaped the communist regime in Vietnam.)</p><p>Others aren&#8217;t that messy and keep their homes clean every day and it might take them a few weeks before it gets messy. They might need a housekeeper to come by once a month.</p><p>Everyone&#8217;s situation is different and the same is true for you with how often you need to keep your projects and lists in check. The GTD book recommends starting with once a week which is a great idea for most of us. After working with some clients, I&#8217;ve also discovered that a weekly review too long of the time period because they&#8217;re so busy and have many daily things to deal with that they needed a daily review. Some even do it twice a day because their lives are that hectic.</p><p>My recommendation is to start with once a week. If your life is so busy filled with lots of emails, meetings, requests, and daily new tasks you want to move to a daily review. Most of our clients find that doing it towards the end of the day helps them stay on top of everything.</p><p>If you&#8217;re like me and you only need a weekly review, here&#8217;s how to make it consistent: schedule it on your calendar and make it a ritual. For me, this is every Sunday at 6 pm. For newbies, it might take 30-60 minutes to do a review but you&#8217;ll get faster at it the more you do it.</p><p>Nowadays I can do mine in about 15-20 minutes. In fact, I have a very simple checklist that I follow in Evernote <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/technology/best-gtd-apps/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">one of our recommended GTD apps </a>so I know exactly what I need to do each time (and not rely on my memory and start wandering off doing other things).</p><h3>Next Actions</h3><p>We have a podcast called The Productivity Show and we just released an episode on the <a href=\"http://theproductivityshow.com/309\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Top 5 Mistakes Most GTD Users Make</a>. We go into more detail there too of other things you might be doing wrong and how to fix it.</p><p>If you want to get more productivity training and my checklist for a weekly review, you have to become a Dojo member. It&#8217;s our private community that comes with mentorship, coaching, and accountability. This is where we help members become more productive every week at work and in life. <a href=\"https://asianefficiencygo.com/dojo-2/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">You can sign up for it here</a>.</p><p>In fact, we have a live Weekly Review training coming up for our Dojo members where we&#8217;ll walk you through how to conduct a daily and weekly review. <a href=\"https://asianefficiencygo.com/dojo-2/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Here&#8217;s the link to sign up for the Dojo and then you can register for this live class</a>.</p><p>There will be a recording of it too so if you cannot make it live, we&#8217;ll send you a recording of it.</p> ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 21 Jul 2020 11:00:17 +0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/thanh-gtd.jpg","linkMd5":"5b5c4038bad46937fb20a73becb18075","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn29@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-05-11-581_271fc419c5946748.webp","destWidth":1024,"destHeight":615,"sourceBytes":160445,"destBytes":103444,"author":"Thanh Pham","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/thanh-gtd.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn29@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-05-11-581_271fc419c5946748.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/06/David-Allen-and-Thanh-Pham-480x640.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn24@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-05-48-514_13bc7a27b655ea19.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/07/gtd-640x511.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn99@2020_6/2020/08/25/01-05-50-163_09fb8e5b38b06029.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317508238},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"Did You Choose The Right Goals? You were all in.</p><p>Now? Maybe you&#8217;re not so sure. src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/wfh-gear.jpg\" alt=\"Home Office\" width=\"1200\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/wfh-gear.jpg 1200w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/wfh-gear-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/wfh-gear-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/wfh-gear-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" /></p>\n<p>How is your work from home setup working for you?</p>\n<p>Maybe you’ve tried working from home a few times, and it wasn’t for you. Perhaps you’ve been working from home for years and love it, or maybe you are like the millions of knowledge workers who suddenly found themselves working from home thanks to the 2020 pandemic.</p>\n<p>Most of us who start working from home start with a less-than-ideal setup. Maybe you’re trying to do Zoom calls from a table in your bedroom. Maybe you’ve commandeered half the dining table as your “office,” or perhaps you’re like my wife’s colleague who does his Microsoft Teams calls from the garage because it is the only place he can get peace and quiet from the kids.</p>\n<p>If you’re lucky, you even have a room in your home with a door you can close to your home office (now that’s a modern luxury!)</p>\n<p>Either way, being productive while working from home can be a challenge if you don’t have the right tools. Over the years, we’ve helped tens of thousands of people with their productivity, and many of those people have been trying to work from home.</p>\n<p>We have found that those of you working from home have faced some common challenges: how do you get your work done in the time that you have, without it bleeding into “home life”? How do you separate the two? We’ve recorded several <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/297-work-from-home/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">podcasts about working from home</a> and have talked about <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/strategy-wfh-pandemic/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the importance of self-care when working from home</a>, but this is a question that comes up over and over again:</p>\n<p>“What gear do you need to work from home productively?”</p>\n<p>By “gear,” we are talking about your physical tools — things like desks, chairs, technology, AND digital tools — things like desktop &amp; mobile apps.</p>\n<h2>Do you <em>need</em> special gear to work from home?</h2>\n<p>This might be a surprising answer, but no! You don’t <em>need</em> anything special to work from home. Many people work just fine with whatever table and chair they have around, and their laptop or tablet.</p>\n<p>So why bother upgrading?</p>\n<p>We have a lot of experience with this topic. Thanh, myself, and other members of the AE team have worked from home for more than a decade each. Combine that experience with the experience of AE customers, blog readers, and podcast listeners, and we’ve found that there’s a difference between <em>living with</em> a less-than-ideal setup and <em>thriving</em> by having a physical and digital work from home setup that helps you be more productive at home.</p>\n<p>It’s the difference between a setup that propels you forward instead of standing in your way.</p>\n<h2>Our Favorite Work From Home Gear</h2>\n<p>We’ve been asked so many times about the gear that we recommend for working from home that we put together this special resource for you.</p>\n<p>It is called <a href=\"https://asianefficiencygo.com/home-office-hero-evergreen/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Home Office Hero</a>, and it is a super-quick, super-actionable resource that takes you through our top recommendations for working from home.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://asianefficiencygo.com/home-office-hero-evergreen/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Click here to learn more about Home Office Hero</a>.</p>\n<p>I am currently car shopping, so I know how frustrating it is to wade through reviews and recommendations, most of which conflict, trying to figure out what will help you and what is unnecessary.</p>\n<p>If you’re building your work from home setup, you probably want someone just to say, “Here is what you need, and why.” That’s <a href=\"https://asianefficiencygo.com/home-office-hero-evergreen/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Home Office Hero</a>.</p>\n<p>Here’s the challenge: there are so many things that help us work from home, we have more recommendations that we couldn’t fit into Home Office Hero. We decided to share them with you here, so think of this article as an appendix to Home Office Hero.</p>\n<p>We’re going to share four physical tools and four digital tools, in no particular order.</p>\n<p>Let’s get started.</p>\n<h3>Physical Gear</h3>\n<p><strong>1. External Webcam</strong></p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16293\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/logitech-brio-2.jpg\" alt=\"Logitech Brio\" width=\"250\" height=\"232\" /></p>\n<p>You might be thinking: “my laptop already has a built-in camera. Why would I need another one?”</p>\n<p>A built-in webcam will work fine, but we like using an external webcam because it gives you more flexibility. The quality is usually better, and you can position it how you want.</p>\n<p>For example, having a webcam lets you use a large monitor and have it positioned in front of you. If you use your laptop’s camera, you need to have your computer in front of you, or you need to look off to the side when you want to look at the camera.</p>\n<p>Here are two options:</p>\n<ul>\n <li><a href=\"https://amzn.to/3fZ5yXz\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Logitech C920</a> — This is the camera that I have used for years and years. It is good quality, works with both Mac and Windows, and is affordable.</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://amzn.to/3jppogs\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Logitech Brio</a> — This is the webcam that both Thanh and I currently use. It shoots 4K video and is an upgrade over the C920.</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>2. External Keyboard &amp; Mouse</strong></p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16294\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/logitech-k570-2.jpg\" alt=\"Logitech K750\" width=\"250\" height=\"187\" />&nbsp;<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16295\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/logitech-mx-master-2.jpg\" alt=\"Logitech MX Master\" width=\"250\" height=\"250\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/logitech-mx-master-2.jpg 250w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/logitech-mx-master-2-240x240.jpg 240w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/logitech-mx-master-2-150x150.jpg 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 250px) 100vw, 250px\" /></p>\n<p>Continuing the “flexibility is key” theme, having an external keyboard and mouse/trackpad lets you give you much more flexibility with your home office setup.</p>\n<p>Since you don’t need to type on your laptop’s keyboard, you can have your computer raised and/or off to the side, and set things up more ergonomically.</p>\n<p>Here are some options:</p>\n<ul>\n <li>Logitech K750 (<a href=\"https://amzn.to/2WVWCur\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Windows</a>) (<a href=\"https://amzn.to/30Ubt9M\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mac</a>) Solar Powered Keyboard — this is the keyboard that Thanh uses</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://amzn.to/3hH87Om\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Logitech MX Master Mouse </a>— this is the mouse that Thanh uses</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://iqunix.store/products/f96-coral-sea-wireless-mechanical-keyboard?variant=30308776837180\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">IQUNIX F96 Coral Sea Wireless Mechanical Keyboard</a> — Mechanical keyboards are all the rage right now. <a href=\"https://shop.asianefficiency.com/dojo/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dojo</a> member Luc recommends this one.</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>3. Anti-Fatigue Floor Mat</strong></p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16299\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/fully-stand-mat.jpg\" alt=\"Fully Mat\" width=\"400\" height=\"400\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/fully-stand-mat.jpg 400w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/fully-stand-mat-240x240.jpg 240w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/fully-stand-mat-150x150.jpg 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 400px) 100vw, 400px\" /></p>\n<p>We recommend <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/202-home-office/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">using a standing desk</a> for your home office, at least part of the time. The problem with a standing desk is that your feet, knees, and back can become sore — especially when you are still getting used to it.</p>\n<p>If you work while standing, an anti-fatigue floor mat can make things much more comfortable.</p>\n<p>Here are some options:</p>\n<ul>\n <li><a href=\"https://www.fully.com/accessories/standing-desk-mats/stand-mat.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fully Stand Mat</a> — this is the mat that I use, which I bought with my standing desk.</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://amzn.to/3eMKH8r\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Anti Fatigue Comfort Floor Mat By Sky Mats</a> — a top-rated and affordable mat</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://amzn.to/2CIVfbJ\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Ergodriven Topo Mini Floor Mat</a> — a compact non-flat mat to encourage movement, stretching, and massage.</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>4. Purse Hanger</strong></p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16296\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tapp-purse-hanger-2.jpg\" alt=\"Purse Hanger\" width=\"250\" height=\"250\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tapp-purse-hanger-2.jpg 250w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tapp-purse-hanger-2-240x240.jpg 240w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tapp-purse-hanger-2-150x150.jpg 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 250px) 100vw, 250px\" /></p>\n<p>An organized desk <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/how-to-design-your-environment-to-make-it-work-for-you-not-against-you/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">contributes to focus</a>, but it is hard to have an organized office when you have headphones and cables all over the place.</p>\n<p>There are fancy and specialized tools for hanging headphones and organizing cables, but Thanh swears by this surprising solution: purse hangers.</p>\n<p>Traditionally they are used to hang expensive handbags on the side of tables and bars so that one doesn’t have to place them on the floor. They work just as well for hanging headphones and wrangling cables, and best of all, they are inexpensive so you can buy a few to use around your workspace.</p>\n<p>Here are some options:</p>\n<ul>\n <li><a href=\"https://amzn.to/39z1hrg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Swivel Top Purse Hanger</a> — The hook Thanh uses</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=16290/%20https://amzn.to/2PdpgDb\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hero Clip</a> — Dojo members Janeira and Phil recommends.</li>\n</ul>\n<h3>Digital Tools</h3>\n<p>Your work from home setup doesn’t end with your physical gear. You can be more productive using your devices as well, and here are some tools that will help you do that.</p>\n<p><strong>1. Webcam Settings App</strong></p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16302\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/webcam-settings.jpg\" alt=\"Webcam Settings\" width=\"250\" height=\"250\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/webcam-settings.jpg 250w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/webcam-settings-240x240.jpg 240w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/webcam-settings-150x150.jpg 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 250px) 100vw, 250px\" /></p>\n<p>If you are on camera a lot, your webcam settings might not be ideal. Maybe it is showing more than you want behind you, and you’d like to zoom in. Perhaps the color and light aren’t quite right, and you don’t look your best.</p>\n<p>Your Webcam may come with software to help, but if not, you may have some options:</p>\n<ul>\n <li>Windows: Change the <a href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-ca/help/17444/windows-camera-app-webcams-help\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">settings in the Camera app</a></li>\n <li>Windows: If you are techy, there is <a href=\"https://github.com/jpalbert/webcam-settings-dialog-windows\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a hack to access a Camera settings dialog from a shortcut</a>.</li>\n <li>Mac: I have used an app called <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/webcam-settings/id533696630?mt=12\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Webcam Settings</a> for years and years. It lets you have fine control over your webcam’s settings from any app.</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>2. File Sharing App</strong></p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16291\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/dropshare.jpg\" alt=\"Dropshare\" width=\"250\" height=\"250\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/dropshare.jpg 250w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/dropshare-240x240.jpg 240w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/dropshare-150x150.jpg 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 250px) 100vw, 250px\" /></p>\n<p>If you are working from home, you will likely be sharing files, images, and other materials with colleagues. In some cases, you might do that with the built-in tools in Slack or Microsoft Teams, but there is a class of app that lets you quickly upload and share a file, and then automatically copy the link to your clipboard.</p>\n<p>This makes it fast and easy to collaborate and get feedback.</p>\n<p>Here are some options:</p>\n<ul>\n <li><a href=\"https://droplr.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Droplr</a>: This is a cross-platform Windows and Mac app.</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://dropshare.app/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dropshare</a>: This is the app that Thanh and I use. Best of all, it is part of SetApp, the “Netflix of Mac apps.” So if you are a subscriber, you don’t need to pay extra for it.</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>3. Waterminder</strong></p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16297\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/waterminder.jpg\" alt=\"Waterminder\" width=\"250\" height=\"250\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/waterminder.jpg 250w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/waterminder-240x240.jpg 240w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/waterminder-150x150.jpg 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 250px) 100vw, 250px\" /></p>\n<p>Between writing tool #2 and tool #3, I took a quick break to get up, stretch my legs, and refill my water. Why? Because the Waterminder app on my phone reminded me.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://waterminder.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Waterminder</a> is an iOS, Android, and Apple Watch app that tracks how much water you drink and reminds you when it is time to drink more.</p>\n<p>You can set a goal for how much water you want to drink per day (or it can suggest one), and then it helps you work towards it.</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16301\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/waterminder-screen.jpeg\" alt=\"Waterminder\" width=\"300\" height=\"512\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/waterminder-screen.jpeg 300w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/waterminder-screen-293x500.jpeg 293w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></p>\n<p>This is a helpful tool when you work from home because it is so easy to just stay at your desk grinding away and to forget to take breaks and hydrate.</p>\n<p><strong>4. Screen Capture App</strong></p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16298\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zappy.jpg\" alt=\"Zappy\" width=\"250\" height=\"250\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zappy.jpg 250w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zappy-240x240.jpg 240w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zappy-150x150.jpg 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 250px) 100vw, 250px\" /></p>\n<p>When you work with colleagues in an office, collaborating and getting feedback is easy. If you want to show someone something, you just grab them and ask them to come to your desk.</p>\n<p>If you want to help someone with something, you just walk over, sit beside them, and show them.</p>\n<p>When you work from home, collaborating and assisting becomes more complicated, but some tools can help.</p>\n<p>A screen capture app lets you record screenshots or quick videos and marks them up with arrows, text, etc.</p>\n<p>If a picture is 1,000 words, a helpful screengrab is 5,000.</p>\n<p>Here are some options:</p>\n<ul>\n <li><a href=\"https://zapier.com/zappy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Zappy</a> — Zappy is a free app from Zapier, but unfortunately, it is macOS only. Thanh uses it.</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://www.techsmith.com/screen-capture.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Snagit</a> — Snagit is available for Windows and Mac, and is what I use.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Next Steps</h2>\n<p>Whether you only go through this list or pair it with <a href=\"https://asianefficiencygo.com/home-office-hero-evergreen/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Home Office Hero</a>, our advice is the same:</p>\n<p>Don’t let analysis paralysis get you — just pick <strong>1</strong> piece of work from home gear to start.</p>\n<p>Even if none of these physical or digital tools grab your interest, look around: is there something about your setup that you’re “living with”? What can you improve that would make a difference? are you doing on your yearly goals? Are you on track? Are you behind? Have you dropped some goals and added any new ones? Have you even <em>made</em> any goals for the year?</p><p>In this episode, we will be reviewing the goals we made on the podcast at the beginning of the year, and most importantly — we will share some tips and things we&#8217;ve learned about keeping and working towards your goals.</p><p>We&#8217;ll also share what to do when a goal doesn&#8217;t make sense anymore. wp-image-15931\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/iStock-1072319340-e1583852527326.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1200\" height=\"801\" />One big trend we have noticed over the years is that there is tons of free information out there on productivity, efficiency and time management. Heck, our podcast The Productivity Show and the Asian Efficiency blog is all free and consumed by millions of people every year.</p><p>More information does not necessarily mean that you execute on it. Just because you read an article about the five steps to writing down an effective goal does not mean that you immediately implement it, right?</p><p>When we started Asian Efficiency, part of our brand promise was to make everything simple and actionable. Whether you listened to a podcast, read a blog post, or bought one of our courses &#8211; you could expect everything to be simple and actionable.</p><p>Over the years we have seen that more information is confusing people. There are a lot of conflicting ideas, thoughts, and pieces of advice out there. One person says you should do &#8220;x&#8221;, Asian Efficiency says do &#8220;y&#8221; and another podcaster says you need to do &#8220;z&#8221; if you want to be productive. When all these suggestions don&#8217;t overlap or conflict with each other, you get confused, paralyzed, and don&#8217;t take action.</p><p>Take for example the diet industry. If you&#8217;ve been trying to lose weight and thinking of switching to a different diet, you might have heard someone say to do keto, paleo or even the carnivore diet. They&#8217;re all popular but have conflicting ideas such as how many carbs you should eat. It&#8217;s so confusing and you end up doing nothing.</p><p>That&#8217;s a problem! Confusion leads to inaction. We&#8217;ve seen so many people struggle with implementing and executing in the last few years.</p><p>So when we thought about how we can best help people, we knew that putting more information out there is not the solution. We already do that with our podcast and blog. We&#8217;ve realized that there&#8217;s a lot of information in there and not enough value to help people EXECUTE and IMPLEMENT. To do the damn thing that people procrastinate on (which oftentimes are important tasks).</p><p>So we&#8217;re going to address that!</p><p>In 2015 we started the largest private productivity community and training library called the Dojo. This is where members can share ideas with each other and learn from other like-minded people. Every month you will also get a live coaching call with Asian Efficiency team members where you can ask questions and get answers. Members also received 6 new productivity courses a year that aren&#8217;t available anywhere else.</p><p>But we realized it was lacking something &#8211; there wasn&#8217;t enough focus on EXECUTION &#38; IMPLEMENTATION. It was the same model of &#8220;more information&#8221; but it wasn&#8217;t emphasizing enough implementation.</p><p>That had to change. Especially when we&#8217;ve seen so many people struggle with execution and implementation.</p><p>That&#8217;s why we&#8217;re excited to announce the <strong>Dojo 2.0</strong> &#8211; the new and improved Dojo that is focused around EXECUTION and IMPLEMENTATION.</p><h2>Dojo 2.0</h2><p>What is <strong>Dojo 2.0</strong> and what does this mean to you?</p><p>Every month Dojo members will have a live implementation session called <strong>Do The Damn Thing</strong> (DTDT). Each month there&#8217;s a productivity topic and we will invite you to join us on the live implementation session. On the live session, we will teach for a little bit on the topic and then the rest of the time we will give you prompts and exercises to EXECUTE &#38; IMPLEMENT live on the call. By the time the hour is over, you will have implemented everything we&#8217;ve taught you on the live call. If you cannot make it live, we&#8217;ll send you a recording of it so you can still follow along and get the same benefits.</p><p>Think of it as a live group coaching call with a big emphasis on execution while you&#8217;re live on the call. You&#8217;re not there to just learn, you&#8217;re there to execute and implement. I am now Swiss too. My background was in Electronics. I started my career as a field engineer in the life sciences equipment industry. I climbed the ladder to director/VP roles in the company that hired me. Eventually, we got bought by GE. I spent 7 years with GE and learned a ton. This is where I became a Lean Six Sigma blackbelt. Continuous improvement/Process improvement took me into personal productivity. That&#8217;s when I put my nose into GTD 10 years ago. Since then from after-sales, I transitioned into sales and have been running a sales force for one of the top 5 CRO which got bought.</p><p>I then moved into a consultancy role since 2018 where I am helping clients to transform their businesses, focusing on all commercial processes. In parallel, I became a GTD certified trainer. Right now I am leading the deployment of a new ERP (SAP Business One) for a UK company.</p><p>When I am not working, I am supporting our 2 kids. One who&#8217;s into the Swiss national U23 Triathlon team and the other one into acting/dancing/singing. My private life is fairly simple either in training, bike mechanics or taxying kids somewhere for a competition or a show.</p><p><strong><em>What is the backstory that ignited you to get started on becoming more productive?</em></strong></p><p>A little be more than 10 years ago, I was overwhelmed with emails. Leading a P&#38;L and managing teams in different countries, I asked myself, I can&#8217;t be alone with my email problems. I started to Google and discovered an add-in for Outlook called Netcentrics at that time (before it became GTDOA). As I was watching some tutorials for this add-on, I discovered that one of the co-developer had written a book called GTD and his name was David Allen. This was it, I was not alone any longer. Guess what, I started to buy every possible audiobook and read all David&#8217;s stuff more than once.</p><p><em><strong>What was the wall or problem that you ran into that stopped you from accomplishing what you wanted?</strong></em></p><p>I was consumed by my work and I was focusing too much on climbing the corporate ladder. I realized that all of this had terrible side effects. Lack of energy, lack of purpose and meaning, not being totally present with my loved ones when I was with them. I was traveling almost every week, spending my life on planes and airports. I needed to ground myself and rebalance my whole life.</p><p><em><strong>What was the epiphany you experienced and discovered?</strong></em></p><p>When I discovered that GTD was a cutting edge differentiator for me, I became more focused, more productive and it allowed me to release quality time so I could build an athlete mindset. My son was instrumental, as he asked me to join him during some of his bike training sessions. Of course, along the way, I discovered AE, its podcast and the Dojo. At the beginning of my personal productivity journey, I did all the mistakes rookies do &#8211; I was constantly testing new apps, wasting a ton of hours on my GTD ecosystem instead of executing on my agreed next actions.</p><p><em><strong>What was the transformation that you experienced?</strong></em></p><p>AE Dojo introduced me to the 12WY. This was the missing link for me. Don&#8217;t get me wrong, <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/task-management/gtd-intro/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">GTD</a> is great but I was missing the feedback loop <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/revisiting-the-12-week-year/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">12WY</a> provides with its leading and lagging indicators. I decided to write a tool from the book which I shared in the Dojo. I am still using it every week. Thanks to hundreds of hours listening to various podcasts, reading personal development books (I am a great fan of Tony Robbins by the way), all of this taught me to eradicate the word &#8220;excuses&#8221; from my vocabulary. As I tell you, this makes a huge difference. I like the Asian Efficiency&#8217;s <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/tea-framework/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TEA framework</a>. It&#8217;s all up to me on how I want to consume my time, energy and attention, no-one else.</p><p><em><strong>If you have one piece of productivity advice for someone who is struggling to make progress towards their goals, what would it be?</strong></em></p><p>Life is too short, what exactly are we chasing? What is the thinking mechanism at play when deciding on what goals to target? Am I contributing to a bigger good if I achieve this particular goal or is this just for my ego?</p><p>Thank you, Yannick, for sharing!</p><p>Yannick is a great example of what we refer to in our community as a “productivity champ” — someone who continuously looks for ways to become better or someone who has a <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/171-growth-mindset/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">growth mindset</a>. href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/case-study-scott/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Scott</a> who we have written case studies about.</p><p>If you are feeling overwhelmed, exhausted, or distracted, you can overcome that and become a productivity champ too:</p><ul><li>Review our <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/tea-framework/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TEA Framework</a>, and become familiar with the <strong>3 Pillars of Productivity</strong>.</li><li>Take our super-quick <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/quiz/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Productivity Quiz</a>, which will give you actionable insight into where you should get started.</li><li>Pick one (only one!) action step and schedule it on your calendar to implement it.</li></ul><p>If you think we should feature you as a productivity champ, <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/contact/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">get in
