+0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Yannick_-Lhérieau.png","linkMd5":"55ce4f0eca142f9d787125ff92488f6e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn5@2020_3/2020/08/25/01-05-11-537_ddc45986ec6f9b0d.webp","destWidth":484,"destHeight":457,"sourceBytes":357863,"destBytes":13810,"author":"Asian Efficiency Team","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Yannick_-Lhérieau.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn5@2020_3/2020/08/25/01-05-11-537_ddc45986ec6f9b0d.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317508240},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"4 Techniques To Improve Your Calendar Skills","link":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=16213","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16214 size-medium_large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/personal-organizer-768x512.jpg\" alt=\"personal-organizer\" width=\"768\" height=\"512\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/personal-organizer-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/personal-organizer-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/personal-organizer-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></p><p>Do you remember the first time you have ever used a calendar to store important events? I was probably 10 years old and I was just using it for my friends’ birthdays. Then when I was 12-13 years old, I started using the calendar for school activities.</p><p>Fast forward to several years (I refuse to say how long) and my usage of the calendar evolved. I am sure that it&#8217;s the same for you as well. What used to be a birthday and holiday calendar, is now where you have your commitments, opportunities, and what&#8217;s going on in your life. Your calendar is a reflection of what is important for you since it shows where you spend your time on&#8211;it shows what activities you allocate time for.</p><h2>The importance of the calendar</h2><p>A lot of people that I know uses the calendar. This is also a tool that Asian Efficiency would always share with our more than 13,000 customers. Even my 74-year-old mother uses the calendar to keep track of when she needs to harvest her crops. I&#8217;m talking about the Facebook game FarmVille. She also uses the calendar to keep track of when she and her sisters are supposed to have a call via FB Messenger.</p><p>On the other hand, I use the calendar to keep track of appointments (personal and work-related), focus time, gym, etc. I do not use it to keep track of tasks&#8211;there&#8217;s the task manager for that. I don&#8217;t use it for bills as well. <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/schedule-management/how-to-use-a-calendar-and-task-manager-together/\">It’s important that you separate your tasks from your calendar events.</a></p><p>Of course, there are levels when it comes to calendar expertise. Are you a beginner? Intermediate user? Or are you an expert calendar user aka a calendar Jedi?</p><p>No matter what your calendar-expertise level is, here are 3 ways you can take things to the next level and master your calendar.</p><h2>4 tips to master your calendar</h2><h3>1. Pick the calendar type you want to use</h3><p>Analog? Digital? Both?</p><p><strong>Analog Users</strong></p><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16215 size-medium_large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Paper-Calendar-768x576.jpg\" alt=\"Paper Calendar\" width=\"768\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Paper-Calendar-768x576.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Paper-Calendar-500x375.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Paper-Calendar-640x480.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /><br /> Despite the numerous apps and software available, the analog calendar or physical planners will not go obsolete. According to <a href=\"https://www.lifehack.org/articles/featured/writing-and-remembering-why-we-remember-what-we-write.html\">studies</a>, you remember things better when you write it down. Also, when you use an analog calendar or a planner, you can see everything at a glance and at the same time, prioritize and organize better.</p><p>Try this:</p><ul><li>for next week, on a piece of paper, write down everything that you need to put in your calendar</li><li>go over what you have written and decide the order it should go in your calendar</li><li>now that you have a better understanding of what needs to happen next week, add them all to your analog calendar</li></ul><p><strong>Our recommendations for analog calendars:</strong></p><ul><li><a href=\"https://www.neuyear.net/collections/wall-calendars\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">NeuYear Calendar</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.plannerpads.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">PlannerPad</a></li><li>Whiteboard (believe it or not, everyone on the AE team has this)</li><li>Bullet Journal (we have a <a href=\"https://customer.asianefficiency.com/lessons/bullet-journal/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dojo course</a> just for this)</li></ul><p><strong>Digital Users</strong></p><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16216 size-medium_large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/App-Calendar-768x510.jpg\" alt=\"App Calendar\" width=\"768\" height=\"510\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/App-Calendar-768x510.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/App-Calendar-500x332.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/App-Calendar-640x425.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /><br /> The three main reasons why users would go for digital calendars are: portability, convenience, and recurring events.</p><p>Using a digital calendar means that as long as you have your device with you, you have access to your calendar. At the same time, you can easily move events by just dragging it to a different date. It&#8217;s also portable in the sense that you can sync your calendar across devices. It doesn&#8217;t matter if you&#8217;re using a computer or your phone, you&#8217;re assured that whatever change you make on one device is carried over to other devices as well.</p><p>It&#8217;s also super easy to share events with other people. Then there&#8217;s the recurring events and reminders&#8211;which can be very tedious when you do it manually. Remember when I shared about my mom having a calendar event to speak with her sisters? I created a recurring event on her phone and shared it with her sisters. I also shared it with myself so that I can gently remind my mom about it a few hours before.</p><p><strong>Our digital recommendations are:</strong></p><ul><li>Google Calendar (iOS/Android)</li><li>BusyCal</li><li>Fantastical (iOS/Mac)</li><li>Outlook</li></ul><p><strong>Hybrid Users</strong><br /> You&#8217;d think that the Asian Efficiency team are all digital users. You&#8217;d be surprised to know that we are hybrid users. Our main calendar system is digital and we use the analog system as our secondary calendar.</p><p>I have a 12-year old and we have a shared family calendar. However, we still list down her weekly appointments on our fridge&#8217;s magnetic calendar. On it are birthdays that we need to attend as a family, school activities, doctor&#8217;s appointments.</p><p>You can use the <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/233-hybrid-calendar/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hybrid Calendar system</a> to stay on top of projects and tasks.</p><p>It doesn&#8217;t matter which one as long as you <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/digital-analog-calendar-system/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">pick the right one</a> suitable for your usage.</p><h3>2. What do you need to put on your calendar</h3><p>This might sound controversial, but we don’t recommend using your calendar as your task list. There are task managers or to-do apps for that. If it&#8217;s the actual task or project that you need to work on, put it on your task manager. If you need to set some time aside specifically for that task or project, put it on your calendar.</p><p>Your calendar may include the following:</p><ul><li>Appointments &#38; Meetings</li><li>Time-specific tasks</li><li>Time blocks</li><li>Breaks</li></ul><p>Why breaks? Breaks are important for you to continue being productive. A tired person is an unproductive person because a tired brain can mean mediocre work.</p><p>Anything that is date and time-sensitive should go in our calendar. Do not stress your brain out trying to remember when your due for your next dental appointment or when you said you&#8217;d have lunch with your friends.</p><p>Aside from that, when you block out these events in your calendar, it means that no one can surprise you with an unplanned event (meetings and such) since it will be marked busy on your calendar.</p><p>We have courses in the Dojo about how to <a href=\"https://customer.asianefficiency.com/lessons/making-the-most-of-limited-time/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">correctly set up your calendar</a> and how to <a href=\"https://customer.asianefficiency.com/lessons/dojo-live-feb-2019/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">rock it</a>.</p><h3>3. Color-code your calendar events</h3><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16217 size-medium_large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Colorful-Calendar-768x511.jpg\" alt=\"Colorful Calendar\" width=\"768\" height=\"511\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Colorful-Calendar-768x511.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Colorful-Calendar-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Colorful-Calendar-640x426.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></p><p>When you are using a digital calendar, you can <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/schedule-management/color-code-your-calendar/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">color-code different events</a>. For example, you can have different colors for the following events:</p><ul><li>Workout</li><li>Breaks</li><li>Eating</li><li>Focus time</li><li>Rituals</li><li>Calls / Meetings</li></ul><p>This way, with just a glance at your calendar, you know which event is happening next and adjust your state of mind when needed. Do you need to mentally prepare yourself for your focus block? Or since gym time is next, it doesn&#8217;t matter which state you&#8217;re in as long as you go to the gym and sweat it out&#8230;?</p><p>Most of the calendar apps out there have the turn on/off feature so that you can focus on one area of your life at a time.</p><p>You can also use this technique even if you have an analog calendar. You can use colors OR emojis/icons.</p><p>Thanh uses emojis on his calendar (digital). He uses the camera emoji if it&#8217;s a video interview, microphone for podcast recordings, and then a star for an in-person meeting.</p><h3>4. Add buffer blocks to your calendar</h3><p>Do not fill your calendar to the brink of not being able to breathe or giving yourself time for changes. Use these buffer blocks to transition and use this time for a quick break.</p><p>You can use a buffer before a meeting to fill your water bottle and prepare for your meeting. If I have a meeting that I know will last for more than 15 minutes, I always use the restroom during the buffer block before the meeting. I also inform my family that I am about to go to a meeting.</p><p>A <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/case-studies/nate/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">buffer block</a> doesn&#8217;t have to be a huge chunk of your time. It depends on what you have on your calendar.</p><h2>Next Steps</h2><p>Decide what type of calendar you are going to use. Then add your time-specific tasks, time blocks, appointments for the rest of the week.</p> ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 30 Jun 2020 11:00:53 +0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/personal-organizer-768x512.jpg","linkMd5":"25df0beaf01dd618cfe9c91b72368881","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn66@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-05-10-949_2f560fa62ba1e4cc.webp","destWidth":768,"destHeight":512,"sourceBytes":53297,"destBytes":34762,"author":"Marmel Becerial","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/personal-organizer-768x512.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn66@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-05-10-949_2f560fa62ba1e4cc.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Paper-Calendar-768x576.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn55@2020_3/2020/08/25/01-05-48-361_646795a15583f7f3.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/App-Calendar-768x510.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn20@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-50-458_89b6a50fc57b9ef1.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Colorful-Calendar-768x511.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn11@2020_1/2020/08/25/01-05-50-366_398360153ecddcb8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317508238},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"Work From Home Challenge Day 2: Your Daily Reset","link":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=16016","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16020\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/cleared-room-desk.jpg\" alt=\"Cleared home office\" width=\"1200\" height=\"675\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/cleared-room-desk.jpg 1200w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/cleared-room-desk-500x281.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/cleared-room-desk-768x432.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/cleared-room-desk-640x360.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" /></p><p>Welcome to Day 2 of the 5-day Work From Home Challenge. If you haven’t yet, make sure you check out and complete <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/work-from-home-day-1-dress-for-work/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Day 1</a> before continuing with today’s challenge.</p><p>You want to start with the right mindset, and once you have it, today’s challenge is all about beating procrastination and setting yourself up for success.</p><p>Yesterday you took the first step towards the work from home mindset by completing <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/work-from-home-day-1-dress-for-work/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Day 1</a>, so now it is time to make it easy for you to work each day.</p><h2>Help Your “Future You”</h2><p>So it is getting to the end of the workday. You’ve spent the day fighting distractions and making the best of your work from home situation, and now it is time to start wrapping up.</p><p>What do you do?</p><p>You have two options:</p><ol><li>Leave things exactly as they are. Your desk, the applications and windows you have open on your computer, everything.</li><li>Shut everything down, clean everything up, and do a “reset” so that everything is clean and clear for tomorrow.</li></ol><p>By the title of this article, you have probably guessed that we are going to recommend option number 2, but I didn’t always think that way.</p><p>My thinking was: if I am in the middle of something, I should leave things <em>exactly</em> where they are. Leave my applications open. Leave my 15 browser tabs up. Have the 8 Finder or Windows File Explorer windows all over the screen. Then when I come in the next day, everything will be there for me ready to go.</p><p>Here’s the problem — leaving your desk and device cluttered is an invitation for procrastination. <em>Theoretically</em> leaving everything open should make it easier to get started, but here is what happens. When you roll up to your desk in the morning, you are blasted with a bunch of information that makes you triggered and distracted.</p><p>Plus, the activity you were working on at the end of the day may not be what you should be focusing on first thing in the morning. It may not be <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/habits/eat-that-frog-most-important-tasks/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">your most important task for the day</a>, or it may conflict with your morning ritual.</p><p>For example, the first thing I do when I go to my computer in the morning is <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/reasons-start-journaling/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">journal</a>. Having a bunch of technical tools, browser tabs, and file windows open does not help me with that — starting with peace and clarity does.</p><p>We call this preparing-for-your-future-you concept <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/habits/stop-procrastination-by-clearing-to-neutral/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clearing To Neutral</a>, and it is a powerful strategy to beat procrastination in the morning by eliminating friction.</p><h2>Enter Your Daily Reset</h2><p>The idea is to help your future you (aka, “tomorrow you”) and make it easy to hit the ground running with peace and clarity.</p><p>Here’s how it works:</p><ol><li>At the end of each day, close down your apps and browser tabs. If you <em>need</em> those tabs (for example, you’re in the middle of a research project), no problem. Your browser will have a function to bookmark the open tabs, or there are browser plugins that will let you save a group of tabs.</li><li>Clear your desk. Put things away. Re-shelf books, recycle/shred random paper, put away dishes and soda cans.</li><li>Look at your calendar and task manager for tomorrow. Is there anything you are going to need? Is there anything you can do now to make it easier for you to succeed tomorrow?</li></ol><h2>Working from home makes clearing to neutral even more important</h2><p>Having a daily reset and clearing to neutral is a powerful strategy at any time, but it becomes even more helpful when you work from home. You may be working in a less-than-ideal situation, and depending on your location, you can only <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/how-to-design-your-environment-to-make-it-work-for-you-not-against-you/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">design your environment</a> so much.</p><p>If due to space limitations, you’re forced to work in a shared family area, it becomes even more critical. If your “office” is the corner of the kitchen table or bedroom vanity, cleaning and clearing everything at the end of the day will make it more tolerable to live for you and your family members when you are <em>not</em> working.</p><h2>The daily reset in action</h2><p>As an example, here is my daily reset in action.</p><h3>The morning</h3><p>Here is my desk when I came down to my office in the morning. I understand that you may not be in a situation where you can have a room of your own to work in, but the concept is the same: desk is clean and clear, and my desktops are clear. I’m ready to get started with my day.</p><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16017\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-morning.jpg\" alt=\"BD Desk in the morning\" width=\"900\" height=\"563\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-morning.jpg 900w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-morning-500x313.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-morning-768x480.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-morning-640x400.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px\" /></p><h3>Mid-day</h3><p>Just so I don’t give the impression of being some minimalist monk, here is my workspace right before typing these words.</p><p>You’ll see there are papers, books, devices, and even dirty dishes all over the place <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/11/72x72/1f648.png\" alt=\"🙈\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" />. You don’t see another browser window with about 20 tabs open (don’t get Thanh started about my tabs.)</p><p>That’s ok! We all need to do what we need to do to get things done.</p><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16019\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-midday.jpg\" alt=\"BD Desk mid-day\" width=\"900\" height=\"583\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-midday.jpg 900w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-midday-500x324.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-midday-768x497.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-midday-640x415.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px\" /></p><h3>End of Day</h3><p>Now the magic. Here’s a picture I took as I was closing down for the night. You’ll see I put everything away (which again shows the importance of <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/how-to-design-your-environment-to-make-it-work-for-you-not-against-you/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">designing your environment</a>,) and my computer is reset and back to neutral. When I sit down tomorrow morning, I’ll be ready to journal, have a quick meeting, and then tackle my “frog.”</p><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16022\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-signoff.jpg\" alt=\"BD End of Day\" width=\"900\" height=\"539\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-signoff.jpg 900w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-signoff-500x299.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-signoff-768x460.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-signoff-640x383.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px\" /></p><h2>What to do if things are a gong show now</h2><p>You’ll notice that my desk is clear and organized, much to my wife’s shock. Let’s just say she did not think I would be able to keep this up.</p><p>If your workspace is <em>not</em> clean and clear, what do you do?</p><p>There are two strategies you can take</p><ol><li>Take a <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/task-management/day-pain-suffering-1-trick-handling-backlog/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Day of Pain &#38; Suffering</a>. Set aside a day (or more) to tackle it all, clear it up, and then maintain it using your daily reset going forward.</li><li>Schedule a daily or weekly “clutter clearing” session to chip away at it until it is clear. Then maintain using your daily reset.</li></ol><p>Both can work, but I found myself procrastinating on #1, so I went with strategy #2. I had a daily time on my calendar for 15 minutes a day to clean up, and even though it took a few weeks, eventually I got there. I found it easier to carve out 15 minutes than a whole day. I certainly would have got there faster with #1, though.</p><h2>Exercise</h2><p>Here we go, it’s time to put today’s lesson into action.</p><ul><li>Add time on your calendar and <strong>set a reminder</strong> to do your daily reset at the end of today, and every day. By the end of the day, you&#8217;ll be tired and won&#8217;t remember, so you need that reminder. You won’t feel like doing it, but once you establish the habit, it only takes a few minutes.</li><li>If needed, schedule your “day of pain and suffering” or “clutter cleanup session.”</li><li>Let us know in the comments when you’re done, and share when your daily reset time will be.</li></ul><div class=\"post-optin-wrapper\"><div class=\"inline-fields short-fields feature optin-form text-center Duncan","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/cleared-room-desk.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn13@2020_1/2020/08/25/01-05-11-429_7ffa12602ac5a503.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-morning.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn4@2020_6/2020/08/25/01-05-50-392_d44ffb7f86451611.webp","https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/11/72x72/1f648.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn55@2020_1/2020/08/25/01-05-49-227_65e30a70f41b57df.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-desk-midday.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn75@2020_1/2020/08/25/01-05-48-582_1eb2a95a9b83eb82.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/bd-signoff.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn59@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-49-837_0be1c583fb9c188d.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317508241},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"The Winners For The 2020 Work From Home Challenge","link":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=16134","description":"<p>We received over 300 entries for the <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/work-from-home-challenge/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Work From Home challenge</a> and we are still receiving feedback about it even though the deadline for the submission has passed. We are happy that the challenge was able to help a lot of our readers transition to work from home. We also received a lot of entries from people who have been working from home for more than 10 years!</p><p>It was a testament that the tips also worked for seasoned WFH Asian Efficiency readers and customers.</p><h3>Here&#8217;s a recap of the challenge (feel free to share with other people!):</h3><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/work-from-home-day-1-dress-for-work/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Work From Home Challenge Day 1: Dress For Work</a><br /> <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/work-from-home-day-2-daily-reset/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Work From Home Challenge Day 2: Your Daily Reset</a><br /> <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/work-from-home-day-3-create-time-and-space-to-focus/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Work From Home Challenge Day 3: Create Time And Space To Focus</a><br /> <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/work-from-home-day-4-reenergize-with-breaks/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Work From Home Challenge Day 4: Reenergize With Breaks</a><br /> <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/work-from-home-day-5-cut-off-time/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Work From Home Challenge Day 5: Set A Cut Off Time</a></p><h2>And now&#8230; The winners are&#8230;</h2><h3>Dan R.</h3><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16137 size-medium\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Dan-Roberson-500x333.jpeg\" alt=\"Dan Roberson\" width=\"500\" height=\"333\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Dan-Roberson-500x333.jpeg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Dan-Roberson-768x512.jpeg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Dan-Roberson-640x427.jpeg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 500px) 100vw, 500px\" /></p><p>First Prize: Bose QC35 II Noise Canceling Headphones</p><blockquote><p>&#8220;I&#8217;ve worked from home a day or two per week off and on for the past five years with mixed success. However, with the situation we are currently in, things have changed drastically as everyone is home doing their own thing. We all just flew by the seat of our pants and let things evolve for the first couple of weeks of the stay at home order, and we were all struggling. My wife and I set up at the dining room table and attempted to put the kids at a table I rigged up from some wood I had laying around. We quickly realized this wasn&#8217;t working and knew we had to make a change. The timing of this happened to coincide with the Work From Home Challenge getting started, so it was a great excuse to move the kids and set my wife and me up at the table I built since we needed a more permanent place to work from. When doing this I had mentioned how I liked my space clean and that I used the CTN (clearing to neutral) method to do that. My family was intrigued by what that entailed. We got into a quick conversation about CTN and everyone was on board to start using it not just for work, but around the house too. We started that weekend with a quick CTN as part of our bedtime routine. The family loved it and that&#8217;s when my wife and son decided to take part in the Work From Home Challenge as well.</p><p>I mentioned in my first post that the domino video Thanh shared years ago was a good reminder of taking care of the easy steps first and letting the bigger steps come later. The simple act of dressing the part for work was a great way for each of us to get in the mindset of getting work done. Each of the subsequent daily challenges required a bit more, but the reward was greater too. By the time the challenge was complete, we all had a solid plan of what we needed to do to be successful that day and how we could set ourselves up for future days. We were able to establish a good morning routine to start the day out strong, find specific times in our days to focus on our most important tasks as well as take breaks to avoid burning out. Also, we all know when it&#8217;s time to shut down and come together as a family at the end of the day, and that&#8217;s so important when we are all stuck working at home with one another. It&#8217;s the little things that we do that lead to the biggest rewards, as they help set us up for future successes.&#8221;</p></blockquote><h3>Troy Knight</h3><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16138 size-medium\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Troy-Knight-500x333.jpeg\" alt=\"Troy Knight\" width=\"500\" height=\"333\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Troy-Knight-500x333.jpeg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Troy-Knight-768x512.jpeg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Troy-Knight-640x426.jpeg 640w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Troy-Knight.jpeg 1024w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 500px) 100vw, 500px\" /></p><p>Second Prize: Apple AirPods Pro</p><blockquote><p>&#8220;I would say that one of the biggest changes that I have made as a result of the challenge has been to conscientiously take more breaks throughout the day. This truly has allowed me to keep more fresh as I work through the day.</p><p>I would furthermore emphasize that I still feel that a great deal of the learnings from this challenge can be boiled down to setting boundaries. Some of the boundaries are physical, such a completing the daily reset of the workspace and setting a cut off time. Moreover, much is mental in nature such as dressing for work, creating time and space to focus, and the necessity of breaks.</p><p>These lessons can also be easily applied once restrictions are eased and there is a transition back to an office environment. As a manager of a team, I have been and will continue to share these ideas and foster a positive work environment for all. I suspect that as a result of the positive results of my team, once this season is over we will be extended the option to work remotely more than the two days we had been allotted prior to us all being sequestered in our homes.</p><p>Thank you, again, for the time and effort put into facilitating this challenge and sharing the material.&#8221;</p></blockquote><h3>Alice Ferris</h3><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16136 size-medium\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Alice-Ferris-500x483.jpeg\" alt=\"Alice Ferris\" width=\"500\" height=\"483\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Alice-Ferris-500x483.jpeg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Alice-Ferris-768x742.jpeg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Alice-Ferris-640x618.jpeg 640w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Alice-Ferris.jpeg 800w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 500px) 100vw, 500px\" /></p><p>Third Prize: The 12 Week Year by Brian P. Moran and Michael Lennington</p><blockquote><p>&#8220;Thank you! I&#8217;ve been working from home in some form since 2001, and I still learned new things from this challenge! My &#8220;aha&#8221; moment was to be more honest with myself and my calendar. While I had cut-off times and buffer blocks already scheduled, in reality, I wasn&#8217;t honoring them. Now, I use my buffer block to once again clear to neutral and transition to making dinner. Making dinner is my signal to myself that I&#8217;m done for the day!&#8221;</p></blockquote><p>Thank you, everyone, who participated! src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/itunes-logo.150.jpg\" alt=\"productivity show on itunes\" width=\"150\" height=\"150\" /></a><a rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignleft wp-image-9545 size-full\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/overcast_final1.png\" alt=\"overcast_final\" width=\"150\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/pocket-cast.150.png\" alt=\"the productivity show on pocket cast\" width=\"150\" height=\"150\" /></a></p> ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 24 Aug 2020 11:00:17 +0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/TheProductivityShow_FB-e1482589435887.jpg","linkMd5":"314389a043fa87c7764d7fb9a53e4d74","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn85@2020_2/2020/08/25/01-05-11-115_684a6465226bdb67.webp","destWidth":980,"destHeight":363,"sourceBytes":32599,"destBytes":17056,"author":"Asian Efficiency Team","enclosureType":"audio/mpeg","enclosureUrl":"https://dts.podtrac.com/redirect.mp3/traffic.libsyn.com/secure/productivityshow/314_-_The_Productivity_Show_-_How_To_Get_Into_Flow_State_and_Make_Massive_Progress_Quickly.mp3","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/TheProductivityShow_FB-e1482589435887.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn85@2020_2/2020/08/25/01-05-11-115_684a6465226bdb67.webp","http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/itunes-logo.150.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn72@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-05-49-191_3de616686d8dfb4b.webp","http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/sticher.150.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn23@2020_2/2020/08/25/01-05-50-320_80c57ad218498494.webp","http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/overcast_final1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn23@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-49-489_c087859209696cac.webp","http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/pocket-cast.150.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn100@2020_6/2020/08/25/01-05-48-325_323e6c883aefdcda.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317508237},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"How To Be Consistent With Your GTD Weekly Review (Finally!)","link":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=16253","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16262\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/thinking-computer.jpg\" alt=\"Reviewing At Your Computer\" width=\"1600\" height=\"881\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/thinking-computer.jpg 1600w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/thinking-computer-500x275.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/thinking-computer-768x423.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/thinking-computer-640x352.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1600px) 100vw, 1600px\" /></p><p>Ah, the GTD Weekly Review. Have you ever noticed that when it comes to productivity, the most robust strategies are the ones that we all have the most trouble performing consistently?</p><p>It’s not that they are <em>hard</em>, they are just things that, over time, get cut for more critical and urgent matters.</p><p>You’ve probably found that it is difficult to get everything done in the time that you have. When you feel that way, it’s just human nature to cut out things that don’t have an immediate benefit (or don’t seem to, at least.)</p><p>We’ve helped thousands and thousands of people with their productivity systems, and we’ve found that while short term cuts may help you right now, they will cause issues later on. In this article, we’re going to take you through how to do an effective and efficient Weekly Review, and we are going to share how to be consistent with your review. It almost always comes down to one of two things, and we’re going to help you with both of them.</p><h2>What <em>Is</em> The GTD Weekly Review?</h2><p>“GTD” stands for <em><a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/gtd-book/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Getting Things Done</a>,</em> which is a popular book by David Allen. As I shared in my <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/technology/best-gtd-apps/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">article about GTD apps</a>, <em>Getting Things Done</em> was my first productivity book purchase back in September 2005.</p><p>I don’t say this lightly, but that book purchase changed my life and led to a considerable amount of career and personal growth.</p><p>(By the way, we also have a popular <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/task-management/gtd-intro/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">GTD 101</a> guide on the blog, and additonal GTD resources in <a href=\"https://shop.asianefficiency.com/dojo/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Dojo</a>, our premium productivity community focused on execution and accountability.)</p><p>An important part (some would say <em>most</em> important) of GTD is the Weekly Review. It’s so useful that even if you don’t practice Getting Things Done yourself, you can still benefit from the Review.</p><p>In short, the Weekly Review is a quick (or <em>can</em> be quick if you follow this article) review of your GTD system and work in general:</p><ul><li>Your projects</li><li>Your next actions</li><li>Things you’re waiting for</li><li>Things you should have captured to your system but didn’t</li><li>Things you haven’t had the time to think about</li></ul><p>A popular idea from the GTD book is getting to a state of “mind like water.” The Weekly Review will help you get there every single week.</p><p>When I implemented GTD back in 2005, I was in awe of my initial “mind like water” moment and the ability of the Weekly Review to get me back there. There was only one problem: over time, I stopped being consistent in doing my reviews.</p><h2>What Happens When You Aren’t Consistent With Your Weekly Review</h2><p>Recently, we recorded a podcast called <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/309-gtd-mistakes/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The 5 GTD Mistakes Almost Everyone Makes</a>. One of those mistakes is — you guessed it — not being consistent with the Weekly Review. But why is that a problem?</p><p>Here’s what usually happens — you are tired or swamped, so you decide to “not do it right now.” You aren’t planning to skip it totally; you’re just pushing it off to do later.</p><p>That “later” doesn’t come. Then next week, you skip again. Then the habit is broken.</p><p>Usually, this isn’t a problem right away. You still have an idea of what is going on, and your <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/task-management/quick-capture-primer/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">trusted system</a> is still trustworthy.</p><p>Slowly, over time, you’ll start to miss little things, and life and work will begin to become just a little bit more stressful. Things will start to creep up on you more and more, and eventually, your system will just blow up. You can no longer trust your system, and to the extent that you still <em>have</em> a system, you are just firefighting — putting out the loudest and most urgent fires, but never making real progress.</p><p>The Weekly Review is the secret sauce of GTD — with any system, things will naturally start to get out of control over time. The Weekly Review is what puts it back on track. Without it, things will just spiral.</p><p>You’ll have tasks missed, projects stuck, and follow-ups not done. You’ll start to have “phantom” tasks in your task manager sitting around that you will never actually do.</p><h2>The GTD Weekly Review Process</h2><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16254\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/gtd-postit.jpg\" alt=\"GTD Book with Postit\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/gtd-postit.jpg 1024w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/gtd-postit-500x375.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/gtd-postit-768x576.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/gtd-postit-640x480.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p><p>I have only one sticky note in my yellowed and battered 2005 copy of <em>Getting Things Done</em> that I added back in 2005. It has “Review” written in pencil. Every week I would grab the book off my shelf, flip to the sticky note, and go through the process.</p><p>Now thankfully, I’m more efficient and <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/technology/best-gtd-apps/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">have some tools to help</a>.</p><p>The latest editions of GTD break the review process into three main buckets:</p><ul><li><strong>Get Clear</strong> (I think of it as “looking backwards”)</li><li><strong>Get Current</strong> (I think of it as “look at the current situation”)</li><li><strong>Get Creative</strong> (I think of it as “brainstorm for the future”)</li></ul><p>Here’s what I do for each section. It differs a bit from the GTD book, so if you are unsure, feel free to start with their process and apply it to your own.</p><h3>1. Get Clear: Tie up any loose ends from the week before</h3><p><strong>Gather all the materials you have</strong>. These include physical documents as well as messages and emails.</p><ul><li><strong>Grab the loose papers</strong> around your desk, in your inbox, the unopened mail, everything. Go through it — is there anything actionable or that you need in there?</li><li><strong>Look at your notes</strong> since last week (or since the previous review). I use a notepad on my desk to jot down random notes, and every time I do a review, I draw a line across. Then I know where to start next time. Is there anything in there I missed capturing to my task manager?</li></ul><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16255\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/gtd-review-border.jpg\" alt=\"GTD Notes with Divider\" width=\"800\" height=\"527\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/gtd-review-border.jpg 800w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/gtd-review-border-500x329.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/gtd-review-border-768x506.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/gtd-review-border-640x422.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" /></p><ul><li><strong>Look at your calendar items from the last week </strong>(or since the last review). Is there anything in there that triggers an “oh yeah! I need to…” response? Capture it.</li><li><strong>Look at your email inbox</strong>. Do you see anything actionable there? This is one area where I differ from the GTD book. It recommends getting to inbox zero at this time. If you can do that, great! However, for many people, that is going to lead to stress and procrastination — something the Weekly Review is supposed to stop. For now, skim through your inbox and see if there is anything obvious that you need to capture in there. Then you can <a href=\"http://asianefficiencygo.com/inbox-detox-blog/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">get your email under control</a> when you can.</li><li><strong>Look at your task manager’s inbox</strong>, if it has one. Is there anything in there that you captured but haven’t taken action on yet? Schedule it.</li><li><strong>Are there any ideas</strong> floating around in your head? Is there anything that comes to mind that you keep thinking, “I should…”? Capture it to your trusted system now!</li></ul><h3>2. Get Current: Make sure you can trust your trusted system</h3><p>If you’ve implemented Getting Things Done, you’ll have (or at least you’ll have had at one point) a trusted system broken down to projects and next actions. You’ll also have a Waiting For list.</p><p>What do you do if you’re no longer sure that you can trust your once-trusted system?</p><p>The Weekly Review is what will help you get sorted and stay there. Here’s what to do:</p><ul><li><strong> Look at your projects</strong>. What is done that you can remove? What can you get rid of? Maybe some projects are no longer relevant. Be honest and ruthless — perhaps you want to do it, but will you <em>really</em> do it in the short-medium term? Does every project have a next action? What’s the next thing that you can do that will move this project further?</li><li><strong>Look at your next actions.</strong> What do you need to accomplish immediately that had been flying under the radar? What isn’t relevant anymore? What can you break down further to make it more actionable?</li><li><strong>Review your calendar</strong>. What short, medium and long term calendar entries are coming up? Do you have action items to prepare for them? Do you want to do some “thinking time” ahead of time? Do you have trips to prepare for? Do you need to get things done before an upcoming holiday? Remember, this isn&#8217;t the time to actually <em>do</em> these things. You&#8217;re just identifying and capturing to your trusted system.</li><li><strong>Review your Waiting For list</strong>. Are there any followups needed? Do you need to check in with/prod anyone to get things going?</li></ul><p>The secret sauce for the Get Current step is to be honest and ruthless with removing tasks and projects. Make your trusted system an accurate representation of what is going on. Not what you wish was going on if the world was perfect.</p><h3>3. Get Creative: What can you be doing to move things forward?</h3><ul><li><strong>Look at your Someday/Maybe list</strong> — is “someday” or “maybe” finally here? Is there anything on there you should ditch?</li><li><strong>What can you eliminate</strong> that will give you time and space to be creative? What is holding you back from really making progress?</li><li><strong>What are some “big ideas” you have</strong>? Now it’s time to really get creative in the Get Creative phase. What are some “crazy” ideas you could have to move the needle? Are they really so crazy after all?</li></ul><p>This all sounds like a lot, but the more you do it, the faster it will go.</p><h2>How To Be Consistent With A GTD Weekly Review</h2><p>If being inconsistent with the GTD Weekly Review is such a problem, how do we fix it?</p><p>First, the Weekly Review will never happen until we make the time and space for it. In <em>Getting Things Done</em>, David Allen recommends blocking out 2 hours the afternoon of the last workday of the week.</p><ul><li>On the plus side, for many people, Friday afternoon is usually more open than other times of the week.</li><li>On the downside, many people are feeling brain-dead and tired by then and may feel like skipping it.</li></ul><p>In our opinion, for most people, two hours is too much. If you can do it, great!</p><p>Most of us need to figure out how to have a useful Review in much less time than 2 hours.</p><p>There is no “right” time to do your review. Since David Allen recommends Friday afternoons, that’s a great place to start, but the important part is to be <strong>realistic</strong> and <strong>experiment</strong>. Try Friday afternoon. If it doesn’t work, try Friday morning before work. If it doesn’t work, try Thursday near the end of the day. If it doesn’t work, try Sunday before the family wakes up.</p><h3>The Two Consistency Killers</h3><p>If you struggle to be consistent with your Weekly Review, it probably comes down to one of two reasons:</p><ol><li>The time is wrong. Experiment and try another one. Eventually, you’ll find one that works.</li><li>The review is taking too long. GTD purists will be angry with me (if they aren’t already) but focus more on the “Get Clear” and “Get Current” parts. Break off idea generation for another time. No law says you need to review your entire week in one shot. Perhaps you want the “Get Creative” part not to be done weekly, but maybe less often. Work in the habit of <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/thinking-time/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Thinking Time</a> once a month or even once a quarter.</li></ol><p>Also (and again, <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/11/72x72/1f649.png\" alt=\"🙉\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /> GTD purists), it may be that you don&#8217;t need to review every project every single week. Some projects just don’t change that often.</p><p>For example, the GTD app that I use, OmniFocus, has a built-in Review feature that I love. One thing I love about it is that you can set your review frequency. So if I have a static project, maybe I want to review it every three weeks. I can do that easily.</p><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16256\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/omnifocus-review-frequency.png\" alt=\"GTD Review Frequency\" width=\"528\" height=\"266\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/omnifocus-review-frequency.png 528w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/omnifocus-review-frequency-500x252.png 500w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 528px) 100vw, 528px\" /></p><p>Once you’ve experimented with your schedule and your duration, make sure it is on your calendar with multiple reminders. When it’s time to Review, you want to know about it.</p><h2>Next Actions</h2><p>Here’s what to do next:</p><ol><li>Look at your schedule for the next week. When is a <strong>realistic</strong> time to do your next GTD review?</li><li>Get it on your calendar and set multiple reminders.</li><li>Monitor how long the next one takes. Look for opportunities to make the process faster and more efficient.</li></ol> ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 04 Aug 2020 11:00:03 +0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/thinking-computer.jpg","linkMd5":"ab58b24e9dd3aa36e60926676b05f3c1","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn26@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-10-569_94eb55ed2581c210.webp","destWidth":1600,"destHeight":881,"sourceBytes":119342,"destBytes":64692,"author":"Brooks src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/pocket-cast.150.png\" alt=\"the productivity show on pocket cast\" width=\"150\" height=\"150\" /></a></p> ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 23 Mar 2020 11:00:02 +0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/TheProductivityShow_FB-e1482589435887.jpg","linkMd5":"7031a603c56de6827ca55a1f3a266172","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn85@2020_2/2020/08/25/01-05-11-115_684a6465226bdb67.webp","destWidth":980,"destHeight":363,"sourceBytes":32599,"destBytes":17056,"author":"Asian Efficiency Team","enclosureType":"audio/mpeg","enclosureUrl":"http://dts.podtrac.com/redirect.mp3/traffic.libsyn.com/productivityshow/292_-_The_Productivity_Show_-_Our_Controversial_Productivity_Beliefs_And_Why_They_Work.mp3","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/TheProductivityShow_FB-e1482589435887.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn85@2020_2/2020/08/25/01-05-11-115_684a6465226bdb67.webp","http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/itunes-logo.150.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn72@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-05-49-191_3de616686d8dfb4b.webp","http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/sticher.150.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn23@2020_2/2020/08/25/01-05-50-320_80c57ad218498494.webp","http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/overcast_final1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn23@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-49-489_c087859209696cac.webp","http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/pocket-cast.150.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn100@2020_6/2020/08/25/01-05-48-325_323e6c883aefdcda.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317508241},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"The 10 Mindsets of Highly Productive People","link":"http://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=1121","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-1132\" title=\"Thinking\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/04/thinking.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"259\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/04/thinking.jpg 640w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/04/thinking-500x202.jpg 500w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></p><p>Everyone has a different idea as to what success means, but at the same time, everyone wants to be successful. At Asian Efficiency we write a lot about time management and productivity, two concepts that are related to success. Look at the successful people around you and you will notice that most of them are organized people who value their time. You might wonder what makes them so successful. Oftentimes, it is something you cannot see on the outside. Do you know what it is? It’s the mindsets these people have. <span id=\"more-1121\"></span></p><p>We&#8217;ve analyzed what successful people have in common when it comes to time management and productivity. While people can manage their time in many different ways, the principles behind it are the same. Coming up with these principles wasn’t easy, but zooming out and with some high-level thinking, we came up with 10 mindsets behind time management and productivity. Apply these mindsets for yourself and become an Efficient Asian.</p><h2>1. Inside-out.</h2><p>Before you can apply time management techniques, it is important to understand the logic behind them. It is not efficient to apply techniques and things to your life if you don’t understand why you are doing them. To get the full effect you have to understand the <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/mindsets/inner-game-of-productivity/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">psychology of time management</a> and it starts with how you think about time management. T. Harv Eker gives a great analogy in his book <em><a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/millionaire-mind/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Secrets of the Millionaire Mind</a></em> why working on your beliefs and mindsets are important. This is a direct quote from the book (which we highly recommend):</p><blockquote><p>Imagine a tree. Lets suppose this tree represents the tree of life. On this tree there are fruits. In life, our fruits are called our results. So we look at the fruits (our results) and we don&#8217;t like them; there aren&#8217;t enough of them, they&#8217;re too small, or they don&#8217;t taste good. So what do we tend to do? Most of us put even more attention and focus on the fruits, our results. But what is it that actually creates those particular fruits? It’s the seeds and the roots that create those fruits. It’s what’s under the ground that creates what’s above the ground. It’s what’s invisible that creates what’s visible. So what does that mean? It means that if you want to change the fruits, you will first have to change the roots. If you want to change the visible, you must first change the invisible.</p></blockquote><p>In other words, work on the inside first and your outer results will be a reflection of that. Having the right thoughts and views on time management will automatically translate in the right behaviors that will make you more productive. In order to improve your time management skills, you must first understand it. Once you understand the principles, it doesn’t matter how you apply them.</p><h2>2. Control.</h2><p>When people think of the purpose of time management, they think it is about being more organized. On the surface level, this is true. On a more deeper level, what time management really gives you is a sense of control and control to decide what you want to do.</p><div id=\"attachment_1125\" style=\"width: 509px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"size-full wp-image-1125\" title=\"Locus of Control\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/04/locus_of_control.jpg\" alt=\"Locus of Control\" width=\"499\" height=\"202\" /><p class=\"wp-caption-text\">Locus of Control</p></div><p>In psychology, you have the concept of <strong>Locus of Control</strong>. What that comes down to is, the more you feel like you are in control of your life, the happier you are. By being able to manage your time and life efficiently, your sense of control goes up. That in return makes you a happier person. Isn’t that what everyone wants?</p><h2>3. Responsibility.</h2><p>The first step to being in control of your time and life is by taking responsibility for all your actions. When you take full responsibility, you are in control. It is easy to blame the outside world, but what that really means is that you are not in control. Remember in the previous point, the more you are in control of your life, the happier you feel.</p><p>Be the CEO (Chief Executive Officer) of your life. As the CEO, you control what is going on and take full responsibility for everything. When things go bad, guess who gets the blame first? That’s right, the CEO. <em>Whether it is the CEO’s fault or not, the CEO always takes full responsibility for what is happening.</em></p><p><strong>The same idea applies to your life. You are the primary creative for your own life. How you manage yourself and time is your responsibility. You choose to focus and concentrate on the important tasks, or you choose to spend your resources on time wasters.</strong></p><p>During times when you don’t feel like you aren’t organized or you don’t like how much work you got done, take full responsibility for this. These inconveniences are a direct result of your actions (which you have control over). When you don’t take responsibility for them, it gets easy to blame external forces. The sad truth is, we often cannot influence external forces. That is thinking with an external locus of control, where you believe that outside forces directly control your ability to succeed.</p><p>Before we can move forward, we have to be able to accept where we are at right now. If you aren’t as organized as you like to be, take responsibility for it, accept it, and move forward. You can’t change the past, but you can influence your present and future. The only place to go is forward.</p><h2>4. Leverage points.</h2><p>What motivates you, might not motivate me to take action. Everyone has different triggers that motivate them. Find what motivates you to take action. These could be:</p><ul><li>Hopes</li><li>Dreams</li><li>Goals</li><li>Passion</li></ul><p>Once you have identified what motivates you, setup up triggers that will motivate you into action.</p><p>Nowadays, we get overwhelmed with things to do and information, and we easily get sidetracked. By reminding yourself constantly of your leverage points you keep yourself in check so you can focus on what is important to you.</p><h2>5. Clarity.</h2><p>Clarity is the driving force behind goal setting and prioritizing. Know what you want and where you are heading to. Not knowing what you want leads to procrastination and to wasting time on unimportant things.</p><p>When you prioritize, you have to know what the desired results are. That’s why for the <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/mindsets/the-pareto-principle-or-8020-rule/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">80/20 rule</a> to be effective, you have to know what your desired outcome is. Or else there is no way you can figure out what is important and what is not. The same goes for goal setting. The very first step in goal setting is knowing what you want and then figuring out how to get it.</p><p>Having no clarity with what you want to achieve is like driving a car in foggy weather. You go slow, get lost often, and you hesitate a lot about what you should do. On the other hand, when you know the end destination, it is like driving a car in bright daylight, with your favorite music playing, and a GPS system guiding you along the way. You reach your destination much faster, it is more fun, and you know exactly what to do and when to do it.</p><p>Know your destination and where you are beginning; the middle will make itself up. With your leverage points, you will find a way to get what you want.</p><h2>6. Habits.</h2><p>Humans are a creature of habit; we tend to do the same things over and over again. You can think of habits as systems in your life that do the same thing repeatedly. To create and have effective habits, you will need these three components:</p><ul><li>Knowledge</li><li>Desire</li><li>Skills</li></ul><p>It is crucial to understand that we operate this way because this allows you to make your systems and processes more efficient. You can’t optimize something if you do not understand the underlying mechanics of it (knowledge). The desire, as part of your leverage points, will put you into action. What&#8217;s left is the skills that can translate that knowledge and desire into repeated processes.</p><div id=\"attachment_1129\" style=\"width: 385px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"size-full wp-image-1129\" title=\"Effective Habits\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/04/effective_habits.jpg\" alt=\"Effective Habits\" width=\"375\" height=\"372\" /><p class=\"wp-caption-text\">Effective Habits</p></div><p>Fortunately, you have control over what your habits are. Some of your habits aren’t productive, whereas some of them are. You want to make most of your habits to be productive as possible and make your <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/025-mike-schmitz/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">habits align with goals</a> you want to achieve.</p><p>Most people are not consciously aware of what habits they have. By bringing awareness to your habits you can start changing them to be aligned with what you ultimately want to achieve.</p><h2>7. Remove inefficiencies.</h2><p>Everyone has the same amount of time every day. Some people use their time more wisely than others. In every endeavor or project, there will always be limiting factors holding you back from progressing, and it is your job to remove all inefficiencies to maximize your use of time. Inefficiencies slow you down and waste valuable time and energy.</p><p>Sometimes the bottleneck is you. You can only do so much with the skills you have. Other times could be something else. Whatever it is, in order to move forward in the fastest way possible you have to remove all the inefficiencies. That could mean learning to say no to things and people, removing people from your life, <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/outsourcing/personal-outsourcing-how-to-get-more-than-24-hours-out-of-each-day/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">personal outsourcing</a>, and many more, just to name a few.</p><p>Find the inefficiencies, and remove or optimize them for frictionless progress.</p><h2>8. Manage yourself.</h2><p>Everything starts with you. To be productive you have to use your mind and body in optimal form. It is key to understand how your body functions for you to allow to take full advantage.</p><p>It is a myth that you can work productively every hour of the day. Not all your energy gets used the same way. It goes against how our body functions because it goes through multiple different cycles within 24 hours. There are times when we can fully engage at what we are doing but also we need to allow ourselves to recover.</p><p>In the book <em><a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/power-of-full-engagement/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Power of Full Engagement</a></em> (<a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/books/the-power-of-full-engagement/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">review</a>), Tony Schwartz explains this concept by using an analogy of comparing sprinters and marathon runners. Both runners get over the finish line but do it in different ways. A marathon runner goes slow and steady whereas a sprinter fully engages in his running, disengages from it, and then goes back at it on the next sprint.</p><p>The latter is how we naturally function. When we are awake we can engage at what we do and then we renew ourselves when we sleep. In order to get the most leverage, you need to fully engage at the task at hand (that’s why we say <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/255-back-on-track/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">multitasking is bad</a>) and renew your energy by disengaging from work.</p><p>Sprinters know what their destination is, engage in their sprints, take a break, and then focus again on the next sprint. That is one of the reasons why time-boxing techniques like the <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/motivation/become-more-productive-with-the-pomodoro-technique/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Pomodoro Technique</a> work so well. On the other hand, a marathon runner is not fully engaged and he is pushing beyond his body’s natural level of capacity which causes unnecessary stress. That is why you will never see anyone work all 8 hours at full capacity. It goes against how our bodies naturally work.</p><p>Thus it is important to manage yourself to keep it aligned with how your body functions, and to manage your energy levels at all times. Your energy levels are the bedrock of getting things done because nobody can get work done when they are tired.</p><h2>9. Your own ecosystem.</h2><p>Everyone can be productive if they are put in the right environment. Your surroundings have a direct negative or positive influence on your productivity. We are often unaware of how our environment and surrounding affect us, but being aware of its components is a good step in the right direction. Your environment can consist of the following components:</p><ul><li>People (<a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/social/roommates-family-and-productivity/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">most influential for your productivity</a>)</li><li>Location</li><li>Weather</li><li>Equipment</li></ul><div id=\"attachment_1127\" style=\"width: 496px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"size-full wp-image-1127\" title=\"Your Productivity Ecosystem\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/04/productivity_ecosystem.jpg\" alt=\"Your Productivity Ecosystem\" width=\"486\" height=\"484\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/04/productivity_ecosystem.jpg 486w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/04/productivity_ecosystem-240x240.jpg 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 486px) 100vw, 486px\" /><p class=\"wp-caption-text\">Your Productivity Ecosystem</p></div><p>All these components are part of your own little ecosystem. What characterizes an ecosystem is that there are different components that all influence each other and work together.</p><p>Imagine you are an architect and you have the ability to design your own ecosystem. In essence, your living environment is like an ecosystem that you can set up to be productive, or not. The people you live with, the city you live in, the weather, and your workspace environment all affect each other and work in harmony. Most importantly, they all directly influence you and your personal productivity. Are they influencing you in a good way or a bad way?</p><p>Fortunately, you have direct control of how you design your ecosystem. Integrate all the optimized components together in your environment and when everything around you works together in harmony, it will push you to be productive. Set up your motivational triggers, surround yourself with the right people, have the right tools in your workspace, and manage yourself. All these factors are part of your ecosystem that will directly boost your productivity. Play architect and design your own ecosystem that will be your playground.</p><h2>10. You 2.0.</h2><p>No lazy person ever became successful. Nor do lazy people have time management skills. However, all successful people do have time management skills and to go to the next level, you as a person you need to go to the next level. You need to become your best self. Einstein put it best, “We cannot solve our problems with the same level of thinking we created them.”</p><p>Start by working in different areas of your life to improve:</p><ul><li>Health</li><li>Wealth</li><li>Education</li><li>Relationships</li></ul><p>All these factors when improved will directly impact your time management skills. Fortunately, there are ways to accelerate your path to become YOU 2.0. Specifically, seek out the following components:</p><ul><li>Mentors</li><li>Knowledge</li><li>Experiences</li><li>Models (see <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/systems/systems-thinking/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">systems thinking</a>)</li><li>People networks</li></ul><p>These will put you on the fast track to become you 2.0 and to be an Efficient Asian.</p><p>Did you like this? 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"How to make journaling a ritual (video)","link":"http://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=10648","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16154 size-medium_large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Journal-Book-768x576.jpg\" alt=\"Journal Book\" width=\"768\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Journal-Book-768x576.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Journal-Book-500x375.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/Journal-Book-640x480.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></p><p>We love journaling. It&#8217;s a ritual for writing about, tracking and recording your life down in paper or in digital form.</p><p>It is not about teenagers keeping a secret diary, but a methodical and mindful practice that actively improves your life over time. We recommend everyone to have a journaling ritual because it has so many benefits. Just to name a few:</p><ul><li><strong>Recorded memory.</strong> By writing things down, you have a record of what has happened to you, daily. This is especially great if you have a leaky brain (bad memory).</li><li><strong>Ability to see what you did</strong> on any given day of your life.</li><li><strong>See and track progress</strong> across different areas of your life.</li><li>A unique opportunity to <strong>align day-to-day task with longer-term vision and goals</strong>.</li><li>End every single day knowing that you did well – this creates <strong>motivational momentum</strong>.</li><li>Helps bring other Rituals into your life through questions and reminders.</li><li>Capture your own personal history.</li></ul><p>As part of our <a href=\"https://store.asianefficiency.com/rituals/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Rituals course</a> we&#8217;ve helped thousands of people with their journaling ritual. We have a whole module on how to build a journaling ritual inside the course and now we&#8217;re going to release the main video for free on the blog. You can watch it here:</p><p><iframe src=\"https://fast.wistia.net/embed/iframe/1mssvri68u?dnt=1\" title=\"Journaling Video\" allowtransparency=\"true\" frameborder=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\" class=\"wistia_embed\" name=\"wistia_embed\" allowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen webkitallowfullscreen oallowfullscreen msallowfullscreen width=\"500\" height=\"281\"></iframe><script src=\"https://fast.wistia.net/assets/external/E-v1.js\" async></script></p><h2>Getting started with a journaling ritual</h2><p>Here&#8217;s a simple checklist to help you get started:</p><ul><li>Pick your medium – pen and paper, or digital. Personal preference.</li><li>Work out how your journal will be structured (examples below).</li><li>Decide on your structure and questions (examples below).</li><li>Start journaling.</li></ul><p>The most common question we get from people who want to start journaling is &#8220;what do I write about?&#8221;</p><p>Well Padawan, we&#8217;re here to help. If you&#8217;ve never made journaling a successful ritual before, then we recommend you only answer 2 questions on a daily basis:</p><ul><li>What did I learn today?</li><li>How can I make tomorrow better?</li></ul><p>When you have to answer too many questions it can be hard to make it a ritual. That&#8217;s why you want to keep it as simple as possible and these two questions are extremely effective in helping you grow.</p><p>If you already have a journaling ritual and you want to take it to the next level, our examples below will help you with that. Pick the ones you like and slowly add 1 or 2 new questions to your ritual over time.</p><h3>Daily Template</h3><ul><li>What happened to you that day (events).</li><li>Outcomes, tasks, questions.<ul><li>Outcomes are the big things you want to achieve for the day.</li><li>Tasks are the smaller steps to achieving outcomes.</li></ul></li><li>Write down 3 accomplishments.</li><li>Questions (all optional, pick as you please):</li><li>What did I read?</li><li>What did I learn?</li><li>What did I do to help my future?</li><li>How did I help someone today?</li><li>Who do I love?</li><li>What am I grateful for?</li></ul><h3>Weekly Template</h3><ul><li>What happened to you that week (events).</li><li>Outcomes, tasks, questions.</li><li>Review of how the week went.</li></ul><h3>Monthly Template</h3><ul><li>What happened to you that month (events).</li><li>Outcomes, tasks, questions.</li><li>Review of how the month went.</li></ul><h3>Annual Template</h3><ul><li>What happened to you that year (events).<ul><li>As important things happen, put them into your annual journal entry.</li></ul></li><li>Outcomes, tasks, questions.</li><li>Review of how the year went.</li><li>Questions:<ul><li>Where did I travel?</li><li>Who did I meet?</li><li>What is my net worth now?</li><li>Where did I spend most of my time?</li><li>Where did I spend most of my attention?</li><li>How did I improve at what I do?</li><li>How have most of my close relationships improved?</li><li>How has my health improved?</li><li>How has to my contribution to the world improved, or my charity increased?</li><li>How has my purpose evolved?</li><li>What do I want from the upcoming year?</li><li>What roles have Rituals played in my life this year?</li><li>How can I sustainably create better Rituals for next year?</li></ul></li></ul><h3>Zachary’s Sample Questions #1</h3><ul><li>How has the resistance shown up today?</li><li>How is my girlfriend amazing?</li><li>What did I learn/read?</li><li>What did I do for exercise?</li><li>What was I focused on?<ul><li>Morning</li><li>Day</li><li>Night</li></ul></li></ul><h3>Zachary’s Sample Questions #2</h3><ul><li>How am I feeling right now?</li><li>What am I thankful for right now?</li><li>How much sleep did I get?</li><li>What did I do really well today?</li><li>What did I improve upon?</li><li>What did I learn/read?</li><li>What did I do for exercise?</li><li>How can I do things better tomorrow?</li><li>What value did I give away today?</li><li>What did I enjoy today?</li><li>What was I focused on?<ul><li>Morning</li><li>Day</li><li>Night</li></ul></li><li>What could have been delegated or automated?</li></ul><h3>Zachary’s Sample Questions #3</h3><ul><li>What am I grateful for?</li><li>Who do I love?</li><li>Why am I so happy?</li><li>What am I committed to? (health, relationships, projects)</li><li>How committed am I?</li><li>What is my intention?</li><li>What is my wish?</li><li>Why am I here? (time, place)</li></ul><div class=\"post-optin-wrapper\"><div class=\"inline-fields short-fields feature optin-form text-center post-optin\"><h2>Join Asian Efficiency</h2><p>Get more interesting
