src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/WFH-e1585788050840.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"667\" />At Asian Efficiency we help people become more productive at work and in life. Millions of people have now transitioned to working from home and are struggling to get anything meaningful done. For many of them, it’s their first time working from home which is challenging in itself let alone with the pandemic going on at the same time.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/coronavirus/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">While we&#8217;ve written about how to stay productive during the COVID-19 pandemic</a>, there&#8217;s another thing happening that&#8217;s making it even harder to stay productive.</p><p>Recently, we had over 3.3 million unemployment claims in the United States in one week. That is the highest number of initial jobless claims in history since the Department of Labor started tracking the data in 1967. To put that in perspective, the highest average for a week previously was 695,000 in 1982. Thanks to the coronavirus pandemic we see a lot of businesses get shut down and people furloughed.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-weekly-jobless-claims-record-coronavirus-unemployment-insurance-labor-recession-2020-3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16006 size-full\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/5e7ca11cba85ee447964b888-e1585788107774.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"600\" /></a><br /> Credit: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-weekly-jobless-claims-record-coronavirus-unemployment-insurance-labor-recession-2020-3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Business Insider</a></p><p>When you&#8217;re concerned about losing your job it&#8217;s even harder to get focused. Last week I was talking to my friend Mel and she works as an accountant for a big luxury hotel chain. She told me all of her coworkers got furloughed and that she was afraid that she could lose her job anytime. With all the stress and uncertainty going on it has taken a major toll on her health, sleep, and productivity.</p><p>Three weeks earlier, she declined multiple job offers from big companies in different industries because she loved her employer and co-workers. “Thanh, I wished I had taken one of those offers because I could be working from home and still be working just fine without worries.”</p><p>Three days later, Mel got a letter that she was let go.</p><p>That’s just one of many stories I’ve heard from friends. The scary part is that this might just be the beginning as economists are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-jobless-claims-report-preview-economy-forecasts-coronavirus-unemployment-chart-2020-3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">predicting a 32% unemployment rate by the end of next quarter</a>. So what can you do to prepare? How can you stay productive during these uncertain times?</p><h2>A Major Shift in The Way We Work</h2><p>It’s not all doom and gloom. One of the best things the pandemic has given us is that the work from home bubble has finally popped.</p><p>Back in 2009 when I started working from home, it was a novice concept. Between 2009 to 2017, <a href=\"https://www.flexjobs.com/blog/post/remote-work-statistics/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">there was a 159% increase in remote work</a>. In 2015, 3.9 million U.S. workers were working remotely. As of early 2020, that number is at 4.7 million, or 3.4% of the US population. With the pandemic, almost all people are now working from home because there is no other option.</p><p>However, many industries were resistant to change before the pandemic. There are so many industries where companies and people could have done their work remotely but resisted the change. Industries such as financial planners, medicine, law, dieticians, real estate, and the list go on. They could have done their work from home and still worked with their clients. Yet they didn’t.</p><p>Thanks to the pandemic everyone was forced to work from home and this also forced industries to adapt. They had no choice but to figure out a way to make a living. The veil has been dropped and now millions of people have had a taste of what the benefits are working from home. No more long commutes, a flexible schedule, fewer distractions&#8230;just to name a few.</p><p>The pandemic will be over at some point (hopefully sooner than later) and we’ll all go back to our “normal” lives. However, this pandemic will give many companies and people a new perspective on what a &#8220;client meeting&#8221; now looks like. Previously, it would have been meeting in an office. Today? It&#8217;s virtual. After the pandemic? It will likely be a combination of both. Financial planners can meet clients on a video conference call. Doctors can use telemedicine to diagnose patients without needing an office. The world will change and people will adapt to those new standards. We won’t completely eliminate in-person offices and visits but the time savings, convenience, and effectiveness of remote work will give many of us options that didn’t seem viable before.</p><p>So what does this mean for you?</p><h2>The Shift</h2><p>In this new economy where working remotely is going to become a new skill, the people that are going to be in the highest demand will be those who will be <strong>productive</strong> working from home. As we’re entering a new recession, companies will be cutting expenses, letting people go, and go remote. Some will go fully remote and many will introduce work from home days for their people to save costs and increase productivity.</p><p>While the pandemic affected us in negative ways, it was a blessing for the “work from home” movement. Post-pandemic we will live in a new world and economy where working from home will become widely accepted.</p><p><strong>But here’s the kicker</strong>: most people don’t know how to be productive working from home.</p><p>They like the idea but struggle with getting things done at home. Just check in with yourself here. Have you found it difficult to get work done at home?</p><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/291-5-covid19-coronavirus-isolation/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">When we ran a survey of the Asian Efficiency audience</a>, many who started working from home for the first time and struggled. Even though they knew about Asian Efficiency strategies, they still struggled! Imagine everyone else who doesn’t know about Asian Efficiency&#8230;they don’t stand a chance to be productive at home.</p><p>It’s not their fault. No one has ever shown them how to be productive at home. Nobody told them the setup they need at home to be productive. Right now, there’s no resource or training for this. <a href=\"https://event.webinarjam.com/register/1/w015oao\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">That’s about to change because we’re going to release a Work From Home training series that will help people be productive working from home in early May</a>.</p><p>I&#8217;ve been working from home since 2009 and Asian Efficiency is a 100% remote company. Everyone except one person had never worked remotely before until they started working at Asian Efficiency (the one exception is Brooks, my co-host of <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/291-5-covid19-coronavirus-isolation/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Productivity Show</a>). I&#8217;ve trained single moms, corporate workers, entrepreneurs and a wide range of people to be productive working from home over the years and here’s what I discovered: everyone can be productive working from home.</p><p><strong>Yes, everyone can be productive working from home</strong>. It’s something everyone can get used to. Just think about the first time when you started working in an office setting. You were young, new to working in this type of environment, and eventually figured out how to get things done. It might have taken you a few weeks or months before you found your rhythm but eventually you got used to it.</p><p>If you ever switched careers, departments or jobs you’ve experienced the same feeling. You enter new territory and it takes a bit getting used to but eventually, you adapt and get stuff done. Usually, within a few weeks, you feel comfortable and can thrive.</p><p>Working from home is no different! You will feel out of your element at first because it’s new but if you do it long enough you’ll figure it out too. For some that might take a few weeks or months but right now you don’t have time to waste. As companies are laying off people and we’re entering a recession, you can’t afford to waste any time on “figuring out this work from home thing”.</p><p><a href=\"https://asianefficiencygo.com/pah-webinar-registration/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">That’s why we’re hosting a training</a> to show you everything you need to get set up at home, the perfect schedule for working from home, and how to focus at home (even if you have kids and another person living with you). This training, which is called “How to be productive working from home (without going crazy)” will be live and brand new.</p><p><a href=\"https://asianefficiencygo.com/pah-webinar-registration/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-15986 size-full\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/webinar-workfromhome.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1148\" height=\"772\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/webinar-workfromhome.png 1148w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/webinar-workfromhome-500x336.png 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/webinar-workfromhome-768x516.png 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/webinar-workfromhome-640x430.png 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1148px) 100vw, 1148px\" /></a></p><p><a href=\"https://asianefficiencygo.com/pah-webinar-registration/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Click here to claim your spot for the training</a>.</p><p>Spots are limited and only available during this time. You don’t want to miss this training.</p><p>In this new economy, the ones that will thrive and succeed are people who can be productive working from home. This is the time to prepare yourself and get a competitive edge above everyone else.</p> ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 07 Apr 2020 11:00:04 src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/light-1603766_1920.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1920\" height=\"1280\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/light-1603766_1920.jpg 1920w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/light-1603766_1920-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/light-1603766_1920-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/light-1603766_1920-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1920px) 100vw, 1920px\" /></p><p>Last week we released a podcast episode on how to build a second brain and get organized. The guest was Tiago Forte (the creator behind Building A Second Brain) and we talked about his system for organizing ideas and information. If you&#8217;re a knowledge worker and are unorganized, <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/310-tiago-forte/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">then you need to check out this podcast episode</a>.</p><p>Most of you are dealing with lots of pieces of information like email attachments, digital notes, and ideas written down somewhere on our computer but you have no way of organizing all that information.</p><p>Wouldn&#8217;t it be nice if you had all your knowledge and information organized? Wouldn&#8217;t be efficient to have everything easily accessible?</p><p>That&#8217;s what Tiago teaches for a living through his online courses. One of the things he&#8217;s known for is the <strong>PARA method</strong> which stands for:</p><ul><li>Projects</li><li>Areas</li><li>Resources</li><li>Archives</li></ul><p>It&#8217;s his organizational system to help you be more organized and creative. It doesn&#8217;t matter if you follow a productivity system already (like GTD, 12 Week Year, etc) because it&#8217;s a separate organizational system. In fact, it complements nicely with any personal productivity system you already have because who doesn&#8217;t benefit from a more organized projects, files, and ideas setup?</p><p>Everyone does! Including me.</p><p>The premise of building a second brain is just that &#8211; to have another brain that can store ideas and easily access bits of information you need, anytime. Imagine being able to find any idea you wrote down, files you downloaded, attachments on any of your devices within seconds. How much more efficient would you be?</p><p>Probably a lot!</p><p>I asked Tiago if he would be open to give a free training session to Asian Efficiency readers and he was excited about the idea. He&#8217;s a busy guy but we managed to find an afternoon to get him to help AE readers like you.</p><p>So if you want to learn how to build a second brain and become more organized, then I invite you to join us live next Monday on Aug 10th, it&#8217;s coming up real soon.</p><p><a href=\"https://us02web.zoom.us/meeting/register/tZEpdOqurTIoE92szKWBzD4jy7k8Otv0rFD4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Here&#8217;s the link to register for this free training</a>.</p><p>If you cannot make it live, don&#8217;t worry! We&#8217;ll record it but we will only send out the recording to those who registered (so we only send it to people who are truly interested). So sign up now before life gets in the way.</p><p><a href=\"https://us02web.zoom.us/meeting/register/tZEpdOqurTIoE92szKWBzD4jy7k8Otv0rFD4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Here&#8217;s the link again</a>. I&#8217;ll be there too and I can&#8217;t wait to see you there.</p> ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 05 Aug 2020 11:00:51 +0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/light-1603766_1920.jpg","linkMd5":"75cbb42195d8ef51fd1156e8bf0094de","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn89@2020_3/2020/08/25/01-05-11-385_3a11fc8652a13050.webp","destWidth":1920,"destHeight":1280,"sourceBytes":551600,"destBytes":122212,"author":"Thanh Pham","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/light-1603766_1920.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn89@2020_3/2020/08/25/01-05-11-385_3a11fc8652a13050.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317508237},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"10 Productivity Tools You Should Check Out","link":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=16168","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16173 size-medium_large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Gadgets-Close-up-768x512.jpg\" alt=\"Gadgets Close up\" width=\"768\" height=\"512\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Gadgets-Close-up-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Gadgets-Close-up-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Gadgets-Close-up-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></p><p><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">We are often asked by our Dojo members (the Dojo is our online productivity community) what tools we use. This would range from phone apps, books, electronic devices, to home appliances (not a joke). Our recommendations are based on how it helps us be more productive. Take, for example, a programmable coffee maker becomes a tool for productivity when you use it together with your morning ritual. You wake up, do your business in the bathroom and your coffee is already brewing. By the time you are done, your coffee is already waiting for you. </span></p><p><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">In this blog post, we are going to go over our top 10 purchases from last year that helped us in our productivity. It might not look like it at first glance, but all these tools serve a purpose in our quest to always keep improving.</span></p><p><em>(We understand that due to the current pandemic situation, a lot of us put our spending on hold. We are sharing these hoping that you might find it useful&#8211;if not now, in the near future.)</em></p><h3>1. <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/kettlebell/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Kettlebell</a> and <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/macebar/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mace Bar</a> ($100)</h3><p>Just because most of us can&#8217;t go out to work out, doesn&#8217;t mean that we stop working out altogether. If you are used to moving your body and you stop, you will feel sluggish and will end up being unproductive. Plus you will not feel good about yourself. On the other hand, if you haven&#8217;t been exercising, perhaps you should start today with basic stretching exercises which can give you more <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/how-to-get-more-energy/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">energy to get things done</a>.</p><p>We all know what a <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/kettlebell/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">kettlebell</a> looks like, but what is a macebar? Thanh&#8217;s trainer suggested that he purchase the macebar since it can be used for a full-body workout. Just like the kettlebell, it comes in different weights.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/macebar/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16174 size-post-thumbnail\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Steel-Mace-Bar-720x400.jpg\" alt=\"Steel Mace Bar\" width=\"720\" height=\"400\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Steel-Mace-Bar-720x400.jpg 720w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Steel-Mace-Bar-625x347.jpg 625w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 720px) 100vw, 720px\" /></a></p><p>You do not need all the equipment in your gym to keep up with your workout habits at home. You don&#8217;t have to buy all the heavy equipment as well. If you&#8217;re worried about space, the <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/kettlebell/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">kettlebell</a> and the <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/macebar/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">macebar</a> can both fit in a small closet. You don&#8217;t need an entire room to store it.</p><h3>2. <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/surface-pro-7-799/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Surface Pro 7</a> ($799 and up)</h3><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/surface-pro-7-799/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16175 size-post-thumbnail\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Surface-Pro7-720x400.jpg\" alt=\"Surface Pro7\" width=\"720\" height=\"400\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Surface-Pro7-720x400.jpg 720w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Surface-Pro7-625x347.jpg 625w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 720px) 100vw, 720px\" /></a></p><p>Yes, it&#8217;s Windows OS and no, we didn&#8217;t switch. What we did do consciously the past few years was to incorporate Windows (and Android) to our materials be it in the blog, courses, podcasts, webinars, newsletters, etc. We understand that not everyone uses the Apple ecosystem whether by choice or due to work. Once we got feedback that we need to add Windows, we listened and now, we always look for a Windows (or Android) counterpart.</p><p>Brooks is our Windows go-to person and after buying cheap (Windows) laptops and getting frustrated by it, he decided to invest in the <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/surface-pro-7-799/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Surface Pro 7</a> and had zero regrets. This is what he uses when he needs to create materials for our Windows clients.</p><h3>3. <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/Airpods-Pro/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Airpods Pro</a> ($249)</h3><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/Airpods-Pro/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16176 size-large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Airpods-Pro-640x547.jpg\" alt=\"Airpods Pro\" width=\"640\" height=\"547\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Airpods-Pro-640x547.jpg 640w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Airpods-Pro-500x427.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Airpods-Pro-768x656.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Airpods-Pro.jpg 1500w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></a></p><p>Were you one of those people who laughed when the first <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/Airpods-Pro/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Airpods</a> came out a few years ago because it looked funny? Well, I did. Boy was I wrong. The pro version is even so much better&#8211;not just design-wise but also because of its noise-canceling feature. The majority of the Asian Efficiency team uses this especially since we do have our daily meeting and also our meeting days. We also record a lot for our podcast, course materials, webinars, etc.</p><p>Going hands-free is the way to go when you attend virtual meetings because it gives you the freedom to walk around. Sure there are a lot of cheap options out there (and I have tried some of those) but the fit is often off, is painful to the ears, and doesn&#8217;t last long. The <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/Airpods-Pro/\">Airpods Pro</a> is sweat and water-resistant too. Thanh had an incident before that his Airpods fell in a cold tub but lo and behold! It worked fine the next day.</p><h3>4. <a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/get-together-book/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Get Together</span></a><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> a book by People &#38; Company ($17)</span></h3><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/get-together-book/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16177 size-full\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Get-Together.jpg\" alt=\"Get Together\" width=\"333\" height=\"500\" /></a></p><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/get-together-book/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Get Together</a> is an awesome book that discusses how to build a community that&#8217;s not focused on metrics. The book focuses on what makes a real community by showing you strategies that you can use to effectively build your community from the ground up.</p><p>You can use the learnings from this book for your own group at work or if you have a group outside of work (non-profit, sports groups, etc).</p><h3>5. <a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"https://daylio.webflow.io/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Daylio</span></strong></a><strong><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> app</span></strong></h3><p><a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"https://daylio.webflow.io/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16179 size-medium_large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Daylio-768x471.png\" alt=\"Daylio\" width=\"768\" height=\"471\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Daylio-768x471.png 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Daylio-500x307.png 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Daylio-640x392.png 640w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Daylio.png 982w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></a><strong><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> </span></strong></p><p>If you&#8217;re like Thanh and you want to optimize your life so that you can function at your peak, then <a href=\"https://daylio.webflow.io/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Daylio</a> is an app for you. It tracks your mood and gives you an idea of what makes your mood sour and what activities would improve your mood. For me, I noticed that my mood improves after a good workout and also when my family and I would go out for a picnic or even just watch a feel-good movie (before Covid).</p><p><a href=\"https://daylio.webflow.io/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Daylio</a> is available for both Android and iOS.</p><h3>6. SSD Drive</h3><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/samsung-ssd/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16180 size-medium_large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Samsung-SSD-768x587.jpg\" alt=\"Samsung SSD\" width=\"768\" height=\"587\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Samsung-SSD-768x587.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Samsung-SSD-500x382.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Samsung-SSD-640x489.jpg 640w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Samsung-SSD-300x230.jpg 300w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Samsung-SSD.jpg 1500w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></a></p><p>Although I use cloud storage, it&#8217;s always a <del>good</del> great idea to have a physical storage to save all your important files. You know what&#8217;s an even greater idea? Have two. You might be tempted to just use a partitioned space inside your hard drive but if it gets corrupted, it&#8217;s more expensive (and sometimes no longer possible) to salvage your files rather than just buy an external HDD. Brooks personally recommends the following:</p><ul><li class=\"ql-indent-3\"><a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/samsung-ssd/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Samsung T5 1TB</span></a><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> ($179)</span></li><li class=\"ql-indent-3\"><a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/WD-Blue-3D/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">WD Blue 3D</span></a><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> + </span><a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/UGREEN-Controller/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">UGREEN Enclosure</span></a></li></ul><p>7. <a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/oura-ring/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Oura</span></strong></a><strong><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> ring ($300)</span></strong></p><p><a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/oura-ring/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-15339 size-full\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/Oura-Ring-Black.jpg\" alt=\"Oura Ring Black\" width=\"327\" height=\"327\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/Oura-Ring-Black.jpg 327w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/Oura-Ring-Black-240x240.jpg 240w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/Oura-Ring-Black-150x150.jpg 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 327px) 100vw, 327px\" /></a></p><p>The only reason why I don&#8217;t have this yet is because they don&#8217;t ship to the Philippines. I just needed to get that out of my chest.</p><p>But why the <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/oura-ring/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Oura</a> ring? When your CEO talks about a tool that he uses A LOT and has contributed to his well-being, you will also get curious. I got curious and did my own research. I already have an Apple Watch that I use to track my sleep and also my workout, but according to my research, the Oura ring&#8217;s stats are more accurate. It gets cumbersome to wear the Apple Watch at night and I often find myself taking it off a few nights a week making my data gathering incomplete.</p><p>If you&#8217;ve been on the fence on what to get to track your activities, go for the Oura ring (unless you want the other bells and whistles like notifications, answering calls/messages).</p><h3>8. <a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/KB-Maestro-Field-Guide/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Keyboard Maestro Field Guide</span></a><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> by MacSparky ($29)</span></h3><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/KB-Maestro-Field-Guide/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16181 size-medium_large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Keyboard-Maestro-768x415.png\" alt=\"Keyboard Maestro\" width=\"768\" height=\"415\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Keyboard-Maestro-768x415.png 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Keyboard-Maestro-500x270.png 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Keyboard-Maestro-640x346.png 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></a></p><p>If it can be automated, we will automate it. That&#8217;s not our real slogan but it&#8217;s correct. That is why we love <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/technology/keyboard-maestro/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Keyboard Maestro</a> because it allows us to automate repetitive tasks by using triggers. We talk about it in detail <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/technology/keyboard-maestro/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">here</a>.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/KB-Maestro-Field-Guide/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Keyboard Maestro Field Guide</a> is the perfect partner to the KM app. Before purchasing the field guide, Brooks though he was already an expert in using Keyboard Maestro. Let&#8217;s just say he learned that he was still a beginner.</p><p>If you are big in automation and you want to save time, get Keyboard Maestro together with the Field Guide from MacSparky.</p><p>(Did you know we also have a course all about automation? It&#8217;s called <a href=\"https://shop.asianefficiency.com/automation-academy/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Automation Academy</a>. We also discuss KM in the course.)</p><h3>9. <a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/Theragun-PRO/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Theragun Pro</span></strong></a><strong><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> ($600)</span></strong></h3><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/Theragun-PRO/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16182 size-medium\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Theragun-Pro-490x500.jpg\" alt=\"Theragun Pro\" width=\"490\" height=\"500\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Theragun-Pro-490x500.jpg 490w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Theragun-Pro-768x783.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Theragun-Pro-627x640.jpg 627w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Theragun-Pro.jpg 1100w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 490px) 100vw, 490px\" /></a></p><p>Last year, I went to a physical therapist when I was feeling a numbing pain on my left leg (after a 10km run). I couldn&#8217;t run for more than 10 minutes because I was in agony. He used a stainless steel blade called a Gua Sha to release my leg muscles and then used a &#8216;muscle gun&#8217; (as I used to call it). It. Was. Painful. But in a good way. It released the tension on my leg and I was able to run again!</p><p>If you workout regularly, the <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/Theragun-PRO/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Theragun Pro</a> can help warm up your muscles and remove stiffness. It&#8217;s never a good idea to workout without warming up. The process of warming up before any form of exercise makes sure that you have enough oxygen in your muscles. You only need 30 seconds per muscle group to improve your performance and recover faster after each workout or training.</p><p>I own a different brand (ExoGun) just because Theragun is not available in my country. Thanh personally uses Theragun Pro.</p><h3>10. <a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/Raspberry-PI-Canakit/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Raspberry Pi</span></a><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> ($35)</span></h3><p><a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/Raspberry-PI-Canakit/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-16183 size-large\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/CanaKit-640x637.jpg\" alt=\"CanaKit\" width=\"640\" height=\"637\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/CanaKit-640x637.jpg 640w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/CanaKit-240x240.jpg 240w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/CanaKit-500x498.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/CanaKit-768x765.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/CanaKit-150x150.jpg 150w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/CanaKit.jpg 1500w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></a></p><p>Before you go &#8220;what in the world?!&#8221; know that I also said the same thing. Upon closer inspection, it&#8217;s a pretty awesome hobby kit that will exercise your brain!</p><p>You can use it to learn how to code, build a retro gaming console, control a robot, and etc. Now, you might think &#8220;how is this productive?&#8221;. The thing is, productivity is not all about ticking off a task from your todo list. Being productive also means taking breaks. I would have to say this is a better use of my time rather than scrolling through Facebook mindlessly.</p><p>I am excited to get my own <a class=\"_e75a791d-denali-editor-page-rtfLink\" href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/Raspberry-PI-Canakit/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\">Raspberry Pi</span></a><span data-preserver-spaces=\"true\"> kit to share with my daughter. She&#8217;s going to be homeschool due to the pandemic and this is one activity we can both share when she needs to take a break from her worksheets.</span></p><p>What about you? sizes=\"(max-width: 858px) 100vw, 858px\" /></p><p>It’s a crazy time right now, and millions of people are trying to figure out how to work from home. Brooks and I have been working from home for 11+ years, and we’ve taught hundreds of people how to do the same.</p><p><a href=\"https://shop.asianefficiency.com/productive-home/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">We’re so excited to announce that right now, we’re opening our brand-new course, Productive at Home: A Course for People Who Want to Recession-Proof Their Careers by Learning How to Work from Home.</a></p><p>If you want to double your productivity while working from home, so you’re indispensable and always have a job (no matter what happens with coronavirus or the economy) — then this course is for you.</p><p>We’re teaching it live over the course of 6 weeks. The training will include apps, tools, and routines that you can use.</p><p>-Thanh &#38; the Asian Efficiency team</p> ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 04 May 2020 16:44:04 +0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/img-product_course2.png","linkMd5":"eb9ef9690a43d8f612318002d241aacb","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn37@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-05-10-852_863b94c4a905049b.webp","destWidth":858,"destHeight":393,"sourceBytes":232668,"destBytes":57910,"author":"Thanh Pham","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/img-product_course2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn37@2020_4/2020/08/25/01-05-10-852_863b94c4a905049b.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317508240},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"Work From Home Challenge Day 1: Dress For Work","link":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=16000","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16007\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/clothes.jpeg\" alt=\"Clothes\" width=\"1200\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/clothes.jpeg 1200w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/clothes-500x333.jpeg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/clothes-768x512.jpeg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/clothes-640x427.jpeg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" /></p><p>Welcome!</p><p>Today is day 1 of our 5-day Work From Home Challenge. Thank you so much for joining us.</p><p>Our goal by the end of the challenge is to give you the skills, habits, structure, and tools to work from home. We want you to be as productive at home as you are in the office (or even more so!).</p><p>Before we deal with all the distractions and challenges that working from home can throw at us, we need to deal with one significant roadblock: ourselves.</p><h2>A piece of advice that stuck</h2><p>Back in 2010, I left my corporate job in downtown Vancouver and planned to work from home.</p><p>Well, “planned” might be overstating it. I knew that I wanted to work from home. I knew that I wanted to take my kids to school, and I knew that I wanted to be home with them when school was out. I knew (more or less) what I would do throughout the day for work.</p><p>I can’t honestly say I had given too much thought about <em>how</em> I would work from home.</p><p>On my last day in the office, one of my soon-to-be-former coworkers pulled me aside with a concerned look on her face.</p><p>“Brooks,” she said, “my boyfriend works from home, and he does NOTHING all day. Make sure if you’re going to work from home, you treat it seriously. If you don’t, you’ll end up being lazy like him.”</p><p>My immediate thought was, “I wonder what my wife says to her coworkers about me,” but then I realized I had to do some thinking about how to work from home successfully. Clearly, it doesn’t just happen.</p><p>The first thing I did? <strong>Get dressed for work, even when working from home.</strong></p><h2>Why dressing for work is important</h2><p>At first, being able to work from home sounds great. You can roll out of bed, stumble over to your laptop in your pajamas or workout clothes, and go.</p><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16001\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-robe.jpg\" alt=\"Laptop with Robe\" width=\"800\" height=\"534\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-robe.jpg 800w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-robe-500x334.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-robe-768x513.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-robe-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" /></p><p>It is certainly <em>possible</em> to do that — after all, no one is going to send you home for your dress when you are already there.</p><p>However, getting dressed for work has three benefits that will make you more productive when working from home:</p><ol><li>It helps maintain some semblance of your routine. If you are switching from working in an office to working from home, getting dressed in the morning before you go to work will be at least one constant. And routines <a href=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/206-overwhelm/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">are a strong defense against overwhelm and procrastination</a>.</li><li>Showering, doing your hair, and getting dressed up is a powerful signal to your brain that you are transitioning from “home time” to “work time.” This is especially important when you are living and working in the same physical location. It may be just a few feet between your kitchen table and your workspace (or your kitchen table may <em>be</em> your workspace), so you need all the help you can get to trigger the shift in mindset.</li><li>Getting dressed up for work is a signal to others in your home that you are switching from “home you” to “work you.”</li></ol><h2>What do we mean by “dress up for work”?</h2><p>We aren’t saying you need to put a suit and tie or your favorite power dress on when you get up in the morning (unless you think it will help you get focused).</p><p>It’s okay and only natural to be a bit more casual when working from home, although <a href=\"http://www.columbia.edu/~ms4992/Publications/2015_Slepian-Ferber-Gold-Rutchick_Clothing-Formality_SPPS.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">studies have shown</a> that more formal clothing encourages deeper and more perceptive thinking.</p><p>The key is to wear something approximating what you would wear to the office. Something that says to you and everyone around you “I’m working” vs. “I’m watching <em>Friends</em> on Netflix.”</p><p>Having said that, stores in the US are reporting that <a href=\"https://finance.yahoo.com/news/amid-coronavirus-walmart-says-its-seeing-increased-sales-of-tops-but-not-bottoms-202959379.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">sales of tops are increasing, but not bottoms</a> because of the increase in Zoom and Skype calls. Walmart’s EVP of Corporate Affairs says:</p><blockquote><p>We’re seeing increased sales in tops, but not bottoms. So, people are concerned, obviously, from the waist up.</p></blockquote><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-16002\" src=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-shorts.jpg\" alt=\"Laptop with Shorts\" width=\"800\" height=\"471\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-shorts.jpg 800w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-shorts-500x294.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-shorts-768x452.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-shorts-640x377.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" /></p><p>If you’re wearing sweatpants or shorts on your next Zoom call, your secret is safe with us.</p><h2>Exercise</h2><p>Now it is time for you to take action. Every day of this challenge, we’ll have homework for you. Remember — there’ll never be meaningful change in your life without action!</p><p>Put space on your calendar to take action on this exercise and the rest of the activities for the next five days. You want to make sure you have time set aside to do the exercises. We appreciate you reading, but reading is not enough!</p><p>Here are your action items:</p><ul><li>Plan what you’re going to wear for work tomorrow.</li><li>For bonus points, set it out tonight, so it is ready in the morning.</li><li>For <em>extra</em> bonus points, plan your work wardrobe for the rest of the week. Then you won’t need to think about it, and that’s one less decision you need to make every day.</li><li>Let us know in the comments once you’re done, and even better: let us know what you’re going to wear!</li></ul><p>(For the record, I will be wearing a button-up shirt from Muji up top, and Uniqlo pants.)</p><div class=\"post-optin-wrapper\"><div class=\"inline-fields short-fields feature +0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/clothes.jpeg","linkMd5":"45f88a1d0dfbc3aa6d4f21bb509aa22c","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn97@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-11-403_3b21a7b5bbcc6727.webp","destWidth":1200,"destHeight":800,"sourceBytes":203288,"destBytes":72970,"author":"Brooks Duncan","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/clothes.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn97@2020_5/2020/08/25/01-05-11-403_3b21a7b5bbcc6727.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-robe.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn23@2020_2/2020/08/25/01-05-48-521_850ee3c327be57d9.webp","https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/laptop-shorts.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn47@2020_2/2020/08/25/01-05-49-357_b3b8f7dba7ce7c8e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317508241},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"5 Simple Steps to Setting Goals and Achieving Them","link":"http://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=1282","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-1286\" title=\"Gulfstream\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/05/gulfstream.jpg\" alt=\"Gulfstream\" width=\"640\" height=\"232\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/05/gulfstream.jpg 640w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/05/gulfstream-500x181.jpg 500w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></p><p>Goal setting. It&#8217;s something that everyone tries to do, but only a few people can actually make it work. The challenge most people face is committing themselves to the desired outcome they like to have. As soon the journey begins, obstacles and hurdles come up, and this is where most people end up quitting. Goal setting doesn’t have to be that way. With a few simple tips and tricks, you can make goal-setting work for you.</p><p><span id=\"more-1282\"></span></p><p>Brian Tracy wrote a great overview on goal setting in his book <em><a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/likes/flight-plan/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Flight Plan</a></em>. He uses an analogy of a flight to explain the process of goal setting for personal success. Most flights will be off-course but they all reach their destination. Along the way the pilot has to deal with turbulence, crosswinds, storms, and lightning, which force him to make adjustments throughout the journey. That’s exactly how in real life goal-setting works. You know your destination and you work towards it, but inevitably you have to make adjustments along the way.</p><p>This is where time management comes in. Your time management skills will determine how well you adjust and thus how fast you will reach your goals. Remember, <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/what-is-productivity/\">productivity is the time you spend working towards your goals</a>. When you make adjustments, <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/goals/the-time-management-secret-that-will-eliminate-all-your-time-wasters/\">are they aligned with your goals</a>? For most people, knowing the destination is not the problem. What holds most people back is charting the destination, making the right adjustments, and sticking to it.</p><p>Here are some simple tips and tricks to make sure you reach your goals. In fact, you can break it down in five simple steps.</p><ol><li>Determine what you want to achieve.</li><li>Break down how you will get there.</li><li>Write it down.</li><li>Make it stick.</li><li>Do one thing every day that brings you closer to your goals.</li></ol><h2>1. Determine what you want to achieve</h2><p>This is the easiest part of goal setting. Just ask yourself, “<em>What is it that I would like to achieve within one year?</em>” One year is enough time to make a big goal a reality. To make it easy for yourself, stick to one big goal. If you have no clue where to start, pick one goal in one of the following areas of life:</p><ul><li>Health</li><li>Wealth</li><li>Relationships</li><li>Happiness</li></ul><h2>2. Break down how you will get there</h2><p>After you have determined what you would like to achieve, it gets more challenging. This is also the step where most people fall off the bandwagon. How are you planning to make your goal a reality? You need concrete steps to get to your destination. To fly from point A to B, you need to know the route. The same idea applies to goal setting.</p><p>A lot of people have the goal of becoming “a millionaire”, but then have no clue how to become one. Or someone wants to have a body like Zeus but is clueless on what to do. That’s why new years resolutions do not work, because it is just wishful thinking. You need clarity (one of the <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/mindsets/the-10-mindsets-of-productivity/\">essential productivity mindsets</a>) by having the steps outlined.</p><p>Figure out your game plan. Start with the end in mind and break down backward the steps it takes to reach your goal.</p><h2>3. Write it down</h2><p>To go from wishful thinking to actually achieving your goals, you need to write down your commitments. You have to tell your brain that you are serious about this endeavor by making it think there is an investment level. As humans, once we have invested into something, we hate losing our investment and we will do anything to keep it. By writing down your goals and steps, you have clarity but also you’re telling your brain “<em>Hey, see, this is important to me and I’m investing in it so let’s not drop the ball on this.</em>”</p><p>From my experience, writing it down on paper or on a whiteboard gives a stronger effect than typing it. So write down your goals and steps.</p><h2>4. Make it stick</h2><p>The destination is known, the map is clear, and the route is defined. All you have to do now is stick to the game plan. Unfortunately, this is another hurdle for most people that end up quitting on achieving their goals. The big key here is to keep reminding yourself of the goals you want to achieve. That statement is worth repeating.</p><blockquote><p><strong>Keep reminding yourself of the goals you want to achieve.</strong></p></blockquote><p>This is the process you want to keep up because it gives you the momentum to keep going. Motivation is a limited resource but it can be fabricated to help you stay on your path. Reminding yourself every day helps with this process. In fact, make it inevitable so you get reminded every day of your goal and you can do that by setting up your environment. Here are five tips to help you making it stick.</p><ul><li>Setup <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/motivation/how-to-motivate-yourself-with-motivation-pages/\">motivation pages</a>. Look at these every day. If you want to be a real Efficient Asian, <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/habits/productive-morning-rituals/\">you make it part of your morning ritual</a>.</li><li>Surround yourself with the right people that align with your goals. <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/social/roommates-family-and-productivity/\">The closest people to you have a major impact on your productivity</a>. Make sure they are conducive to you. Many readers accomplish this inside our productivity community, <a href=\"https://shop.asianefficiency.com/dojo\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Dojo</a>. Sometimes it&#8217;s hard when we don&#8217;t have others in our family or life who have the same level of focus. It helps to be with your people, and online communities can help here.</li><li>Create your ecosystem that is aligned with your goals. Your environment, besides the people, also help to make it stick. <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/mindsets/the-10-mindsets-of-productivity/\">See #8 of our 10 essential productivity mindsets</a>.</li><li>Create a desktop background on your laptop or computer with the desired outcomes.</li><li>On your whiteboard (if you don’t have one, you should get one), write down your big goals.</li></ul><p>Setup your environment so that it is <strong>inevitable</strong> that you will never lose your eye on the prize. This does not take a lot of effort but will dramatically increase your chances of succeeding.</p><h2>5. Do one thing every day that brings you closer to your goals</h2><p>How do you make sure that you will reach your goals? Work on them every single day. Yes, every single day. No matter if it is only ten minutes or two hours. Work on your goals every single day so it is inevitable you will get what you want. Use the compound effect in your favor; the earlier you start, the bigger the changes become as time goes by. And the more time you spend working towards your goals, the faster you will achieve them. If you want to be an Efficient Asian, you make them <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/habits/eat-that-frog-most-important-tasks-morning/\">your most important tasks</a>.</p><p>That is really it to goal setting. Implement these 5 simple steps and you will get what you desire. Let me ask you this, what are some of your goals you want to achieve? Leave a comment behind and we will help you achieve them.</p><p>Did you like this? Then you&#8217;ll love our free <a href=\"https://event.webinarjam.com/register/2/rm9rqb8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Asian Efficiency training</a>. It&#8217;s completely free and we&#8217;ll show you our top productivity hacks that helped us save hours. <a href=\"https://event.webinarjam.com/register/2/rm9rqb8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for the next available time slot</a>.</p><p class=\"credit\">Photo by <a href=\"http://www.flickr.com/photos/global-jet/654169387/\">Global Jet</a>.</p> /></p><p>We all know that you can&#8217;t buy your way to productivity. 09:05:08","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 09:05:08","title":"Your Perfect Week Starts With 4 Easy-To-Follow Steps","link":"http://www.asianefficiency.com/?p=15936","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-15937\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Woman-reviewing-week-500x333.jpg\" alt=\"Woman reviewing week\" width=\"1000\" height=\"667\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Woman-reviewing-week-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Woman-reviewing-week-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Woman-reviewing-week-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /><br /> An unproductive year may have started with an unproductive day that turned into a bad week that morphed into an unproductive month that spiraled out of control and became an unproductive year. You didn&#8217;t reach any goals that you&#8217;ve set out to do for the year. Just thinking about it gives me goosebumps.</p><p>That&#8217;s a nightmare that you don&#8217;t have to worry about because Asian Efficiency has helped over 13,000 people avoid that nightmare.</p><p>You might have experienced the &#8220;where did my week go&#8221; problem where you ended your week without making any real progress on your goals or priorities. Worse, your todo list is a rehash of the previous week&#8211;plus more!</p><p>What could you have done better to avoid this?</p><p>The key to having a productive week is not about what you do daily but what you do before the week starts. Plan. You need to plan for your perfect week.</p><h2>How to plan for your perfect week</h2><h3>1. Choose when to do your planning and stick to it</h3><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-15939\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Choosing-date.jpg\" alt=\"Choosing date\" width=\"1000\" height=\"667\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Choosing-date.jpg 2121w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Choosing-date-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Choosing-date-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Choosing-date-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></p><p>This is a crucial part when it comes to planning your week. You cannot just plan when you have time. You have to make time for it and make it as part of your ritual. Sticking to it every single week is one recipe for your success.</p><p>What works for me might not be the best for you. In choosing when to plan, it should be a day and time that you can consistently carve just for your weekly planning.</p><p>In my case, I do it every Sunday night, after dinner. This is usually the quietest part of my week and when everything at home has calmed down. Brooks does his planning every Sunday morning while Thanh does his Sunday afternoon. Others do it on a Saturday and some even during weekdays. What matters most is that you stick to it every single week.</p><p>Start with 30 minutes and eventually increase to 60 minutes. Think of it as your weekly <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/162-thinking-time/\">thinking time</a> where you can reflect on the week that just ended and plan for the week that&#8217;s about to start. This requires you to be present so make sure you are free from distractions. <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/plan-week-ceo/\">You can read about how Thanh plans his week as Asian Efficiency&#8217;s CEO here.</a></p><h3>2. Schedule what&#8217;s important for your week</h3><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-15938\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Planning-Week.jpg\" alt=\"Planning Week\" width=\"1000\" height=\"668\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Planning-Week.jpg 2119w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Planning-Week-500x334.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Planning-Week-768x513.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Planning-Week-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></p><p>If it&#8217;s not in your <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/schedule-management/how-to-use-your-calendar/\">calendar</a>, it probably will not happen because you will end up forgetting about it. During your weekly planning, think about all your <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/productivity/prioritize-todo-list/\">priorities</a> for the week, list them down, and add them to your calendar so that you consciously make time for it. Your calendar is a powerful tool that when used correctly, will help you achieve your goals.</p><p>It&#8217;s easy to miss important tasks when you don&#8217;t have a visual (whether analog or digital) reminder of it. It happened to me several times before&#8211;like forgetting to carve out time to pick up my daughter&#8217;s report card (oops) and her parent-teacher 1on1 (double oops).</p><p>When something unexpected pops up during the week, you can immediately look at your calendar and decide what you can move or not move to accommodate this surprise. You don&#8217;t have to panic since you have everything in place&#8211;you just have to move some pieces around.</p><h3>3. Review your previous week</h3><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-15940\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Weekly-Review.jpg\" alt=\"Weekly Review\" width=\"1000\" height=\"667\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Weekly-Review.jpg 2121w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Weekly-Review-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Weekly-Review-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Weekly-Review-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></p><p>The review process is vital for you to make the necessary adjustments and improvements to your weekly planning. Here are some questions you can ask during the review process:</p><ul><li>What went well?</li><li>What didn&#8217;t go well?</li><li>What can be better?</li><li>What improvements can I make?</li></ul><p>Those are just some questions you can use. Of course, feel free to add to it if it helps in your review.</p><p>It&#8217;s during this step that I realized how important it was to add all time-bound activities to my calendar because I tend to forget if I just file it inside my head.</p><p>It&#8217;s going to be useless to do a review if you do not do anything about it after. You can immediately make changes to your plans during your review</p><h3>4. Leave some room for surprises</h3><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-15941\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Surprises-and-emergencies.jpg\" alt=\"Surprises and emergencies\" width=\"1000\" height=\"667\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Surprises-and-emergencies.jpg 2121w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Surprises-and-emergencies-500x333.jpg 500w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Surprises-and-emergencies-768x512.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Surprises-and-emergencies-640x427.jpg 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></p><p>Whether you like it or not, it&#8217;s bound to happen every week. There are things you can control, but there are also a lot of things you can&#8217;t control especially if it involves other people (even technology).</p><p>Don&#8217;t go overboard and fill your calendar with things to do every 30 minutes&#8211;that&#8217;s overkill. Have enough <a href=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/podcast/288-12-week-year/\">buffer time</a> that will allow you to accommodate any surprises that may arise.</p><p>Meeting a friend for lunch? Make it 3 hours instead of 2. Doing errands for the day? Make it 2 hours instead of 1. Going to the gym? I put in 2 hours even if it usually takes me an hour because there are times when traffic is bad or the gym is full.</p><p>Having this extra room to wiggle ensures that you don&#8217;t panic and end up canceling out on your priorities.</p><h2>Next Steps</h2><p>These 4 steps are pretty simple and easy to follow. The key is consistency in doing it. Find out what day and time is best to do your planning and do it. List down your priorities and add those to your calendar while making sure that you have enough buffer time for surprises.</p> ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 31 Mar 2020 11:00:59 sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></p><p>Asian Efficiency is known for sharing productivity tips that we personally use because we are confident that it will help you out too. We have helped over 13000 people (maybe you are one of them!) take back their time and helped them focus on what was important.</p><p>This is why we are going to share 10 of our favorite tools that will not only help with your productivity but will also make your life a little bit more convenient and it won&#8217;t break the bank. You might still want to either get your wallet ready or make sure it&#8217;s far away from you.</p><p>These tools have been tried and tested by some (if not all) of the Asian Efficiency team. We will not be discussing apps because we already have a ton of that in the blog.</p><h2>Asian Efficiency&#8217;s Top 10 Tools Below $100</h2><h3>1. <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B07D33RMRN/?tag=asianeffic-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">HyperDrive USB C Hub &#8211; $89</a></h3><p>Technology is constantly evolving and sometimes, some of our tools are not always compatible or is late to the evolving game. One example would be the new MacBook Pro which has USB-C ports and does not have any USB-A port at all. Now, if you connect a lot of stuff to your laptop using the old USB port, it can be quite frustrating since you would have to use a lot of dongles (think of your ethernet cable, printer cable, flash drives, external HDD, at a lot more). It&#8217;s not only an eyesore, it&#8217;s also a recipe for &#8220;<em>Oh my, I left my dongle at home!&#8221;</em></p><p>The HyperDrive USB C Hub is perfect for the new MacBookPro because it attaches itself beautifully (yes, this is how I&#8217;m going to describe it since the opposite is just ugly) to the side of your MBP. I mean&#8211;look at it!</p><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-15448\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/HyperDrive-e1568042213413.jpg\" alt=\"HyperDrive\" width=\"1000\" height=\"1000\" /></p><p>It occupies two USB-C ports and before you go, what?!?!?! Don&#8217;t worry about it because the hub contains:</p><ul><li>2 USB-C ports (makes up for the two it occupies!)</li><li>Gigabit Ethernet Port</li><li>HDMI</li><li>SD</li><li>Micro SD</li><li>USB-A (hooray!)</li><li>Thunderbolt 3</li></ul><p>You can always purchase two and put one in your laptop bag for good measure.</p><h3>2. <a href=\"http://aelikes.com/c/s/ssz/P/5/zNZ/P/6TUInT/6jV0urZf8l/P/P/P\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Gunnar glasses &#8211; $50</a></h3><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-15452\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Gunnar-Glasses-e1568042290942.jpg\" alt=\"Gunnar Glasses\" width=\"1000\" height=\"445\" /></p><p>Tell me of a day that you were not able to look at a screen? It could be a TV, computer, mobile phone, tablet&#8230; I think I haven&#8217;t gone on a &#8220;screen-less&#8221; day for the past 20 years. I earned a degree in computer programming so since I was in college, my face was basically in front of a computer every single day.</p><p>Now that we are (hopefully) more informed, we know that screens emit Bluelight that&#8217;s harmful to our retina, cataracts, and also increases your risk of getting a sleeping disorder.</p><p>There&#8217;s a reason why we always tell our readers that if you need to sleep make sure you stop using the computer or your phone an hour before bedtime&#8211;it&#8217;s the Bluelight.</p><p>But what if you don&#8217;t have that one hour? Since I work night shifts, I am directly in front of the computer up until I log out and then sleep. It&#8217;s a great thing that Thanh gave me a pair because it has been a lifesaver (or sleep saver). Right now, even if I am using my computer until the last minute before hitting the sack, I don&#8217;t have trouble falling asleep. Before, I would toss and turn for at least 30 minutes before I would finally fall asleep. We all know that sleep is a very important factor when it comes to productivity.</p><p>Aside from blocking harmful Bluelight and UV light, it also reduces eye strain. When you are facing the computer for at least 4 hours a day&#8211;you know what I am talking about.</p><h3>3. <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Contigo-AUTOSEAL-Vaccuum-Insulated-Stainless-Travel/dp/B00HZI5XBG/?tag=asianeffic-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Contigo AUTOSEAL West Loop Stainless Steel Travel Mug &#8211; $15</a></h3><p><img class=\"alignnone size-large wp-image-15446\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Contigo-471x640.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"471\" height=\"640\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Contigo-471x640.jpg 471w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Contigo-368x500.jpg 368w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Contigo-768x1043.jpg 768w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Contigo.jpg 1105w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 471px) 100vw, 471px\" /></p><p>Before you say &#8220;I don&#8217;t need another travel mug&#8221;, hear me out. You will never appreciate the importance of having an auto seal travel mug until such time that you end up with coffee on your pants or your shirt.</p><p>Yes. It&#8217;s AUTO SEAL. Meaning, after you take a sip, it auto seals itself. You don&#8217;t need two hands to drink and close since you only need to press one button. If you don&#8217;t press the button, no liquid will come out.</p><p>You only need to make sure that you close it properly when you fill it up and you can put it inside your bag without worrying that it&#8217;s going to spill.</p><p>Hot drinks stay hot for 5 hours and then 12 hours for cold drinks. It comes in three sizes and more than 15 colors.</p><h3>4. Electrolyte powders &#8211; $20</h3><p>As morbid as it sounds, dehydration is a silent killer. It&#8217;s also bad for your productivity since it lowers down your output. Did you know that if you are dehydrated even by just 3%-4%, your productivity is lowered down to 25%-50%? Mental ability or performance also decreases. This is also the same when you engage in physical activities like sports or when you regularly work out. If you are dehydrated, your physical performance also suffers.</p><p>So if you want to stay on top of your productivity and maintain peak physical performance, you need to keep yourself hydrated and electrolyte powders can help you with this.</p><p>Electrolytes not only make the most of your water, it also helps your body maintain its proper functions. If you get bored drinking plain water (trust me, there are people like that), then electrolyte powders can help since it&#8217;s flavored. Thanh&#8217;s favorite brands are <a href=\"http://aelikes.com/c/s/ssz/P/Y/zCx/P/6TUInT/UW5aI6IcH1/P/P/P\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Vega Sports Hydrator</a> and <a href=\"http://aelikes.com/c/s/ssz/P/e/UdH/P/6TUInT/sSuBLN58Vw/P/P/P\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">LMNT</a>.</p><p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-15451 size-large\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Vega-Hydrator-451x640.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"451\" height=\"640\" srcset=\"https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Vega-Hydrator-451x640.jpg 451w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Vega-Hydrator-352x500.jpg 352w, https://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Vega-Hydrator.jpg 733w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 451px) 100vw, 451px\" /></p><h3>5. <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Gerber-Dime-Multi-Tool-Black-30-000469/dp/B006M9NIDO/?tag=asianeffic-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Gerber Dime Multi-Tool &#8211; $20</a></h3><p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-15447\" src=\"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/Gerber-e1568042458959.jpg\" alt=\"Gerber\" width=\"1000\" height=\"1000\" /></p><p>Be like MacGyver by getting this multi-tool that has needle-nose spring-loaded pliers, wirecutter, fine-edge blade, retail package opener, scissors, medium flat driver, crosshead driver, bottle opener, tweezers, and a file. ","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 17 Aug 2020 11:00:07 +0000","feedId":10782,"bgimg":"http://www.asianefficiency.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/TheProductivityShow_FB-e1482589435887.jpg","linkMd5":"0e2bf67590540ccda45f6b0a612113d6","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn85@2020_2/2020/08/25/01-05-11-115_684a6465226bdb67.webp","destWidth":980,"destHeight":363,"sourceBytes":32599,"destBytes":17056,"author":"Asian
